Transmitted Evidence for the Permissibility of Seeing Allah
Nasafi presents Quranic verses and hadith as evidence for ru'ya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key transmitted (naqli) evidences Nasafi uses to argue for the permissibility of seeing Allah (ru'ya) in the Hereafter, including Quranic verses and hadith, and how he addresses potential misinterpretations.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah is possible: Quran and hadith affirm it with clear proofs.

Nasafi now turns from rational proofs to transmitted (samii) evidences. The Quran explicitly states that believers will look at their Lord, and the Prophet's Companions unanimously narrated the hadith of ru'ya. This lesson examines the two key verses and the support from the Companions' consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice how Nasafi cites verses and then supports with the number of Companions.
Pay attention to the key terms: رؤية, نظر, زيادة.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
Find the verses from al-Qiyama and Yunus. Understand Nasafi's argument that الناظرة means looking, not waiting.
He uses grammar and poetry to support his interpretation.
3
Consider the hadith evidence
Nasafi mentions 21 Companions narrated the hadith of ru'ya. This shows the strength of the transmitted evidence.
He confirms they are trustworthy (thiqat).
4
Reflect on the significance
Why is it important that the evidence is both Quranic and hadith? How does this support the Ahl al-Sunna position?
This counters those who deny ru'ya based on other verses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْ كَلَامِ النَّسَفِيِّ أَيْضًا عَلَى جَوَازِ رُؤْيَتِهِ تَعَالَى قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَئِذٍ نَاضِرَةٌ * إِلَى رَبِّهَا نَاظِرَةٌ} [القيامة: ٢٢، ٢٣]، وَيَعْرِضُ النَّسَفِيُّ الْكَلَامَ حَوْلَ هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ بِالتَّفْصِيلِ، مُسْتَشْهِدًا بِكَلَامِ النَّحْوِيِّينَ وَالشُّعَرَاءِ، مُثْبِتًا أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِهَا النَّظَرُ لَا الِانْتِظَارُ. وَأَيْضًا مِنَ الْأَدِلَّةِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {لِلَّذِينَ أَحْسَنُوا الْحُسْنَى وَزِيَادَةٌ} [يُونُسَ: ٢٦] وَقَدْ رُوِيَ فِي خَبَرٍ أَنَّ الزِّيَادَةَ هِيَ النَّظَرُ إِلَى اللهِ تَعَالَى، وَيَدْعَمُ كَلَامَهُ بِأَنَّ وَاحِدًا وَعِشْرِينَ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ الْأَجِلَّاءِ رَوَوْا حَدِيثَ الرُّؤْيَةِ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ وَيَذْكُرُهُمْ بِأَسْمَائِهِمْ، وَقَدْ بَحَثْتُ عَنْهُمْ جَمِيعًا فَوَجَدْتُ أَنَّهُمْ ثِقَاتٌ كَمَا هُوَ مُبَيَّنٌ فِي التَّحْقِيقِ.
And from the words of al-Nasafi also on the permissibility of seeing Him (Exalted) is His statement: 'Faces on that day will be radiant, looking at their Lord' [al-Qiyama 22-23]. And al-Nasafi discusses this verse in detail, citing the words of grammarians and poets, affirming that the intended meaning is 'looking' not 'waiting'. And also from the evidences is His statement: 'For those who do good is the best (reward) and more' [Yunus 26], and it has been narrated in a report that 'the more' is looking at Allah (Exalted). And he supports his statement that twenty-one of the noble Companions narrated the hadith of ru'ya (vision) from the Messenger of Allah, and he mentions them by name, and I have researched all of them and found them to be trustworthy, as is explained in the verification.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents the transmitted (naqli) evidence for the permissibility of seeing Allah (ru'ya) in the Hereafter. Nasafi begins by citing the Quranic verse from Surah al-Qiyama: 'Faces on that day will be radiant, looking at their Lord.' He then explains that he discusses this verse in detail, using the statements of grammarians and poets to prove that the word 'nazira' here means 'looking' (ru'ya) and not 'waiting' (intizar). Next, he cites another verse from Surah Yunus: 'For those who do good is the best (reward) and more,' and notes a report that interprets 'the more' as looking at Allah. Finally, he supports his argument by mentioning that twenty-one noble Companions narrated the hadith of ru'ya from the Prophet, and he names them, confirming that they are all trustworthy (thiqat).

Key Terms
رؤية
نظر
زيادة
صحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some interpret the verse 'إلى ربها ناظرة' as meaning 'waiting for their Lord' rather than 'looking at their Lord'.
Correction: Nasafi, using grammatical and poetic evidence, affirms that the intended meaning is actual vision (ru'ya), not waiting.

Checkpoint
Which two Quranic verses does Nasafi cite as evidence for the permissibility of seeing Allah?
A) Surah al-Qiyama 22-23 and Surah Yunus 26
B) Surah al-An'am 103 and Surah al-Qiyama 22-23
C) Surah Yunus 26 and Surah al-An'am 103
D) Surah al-Qiyama 22-23 and Surah al-Baqara 255

Key Takeaway
The Quran and the consensus of the Companions provide strong transmitted evidence for the permissibility of seeing Allah in the Hereafter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'إلى ربها ناظرة' (looking at their Lord), does your heart yearn for that moment? What in your life today distracts you from longing to see Allah?
?
The companions were so certain of ru'ya that 21 of them narrated it. Are you as certain of the unseen as they were? What would change in your actions if you truly believed you will see your Lord?
?
Nasafi used grammarians and poets to prove the meaning. Have you ever studied the Quran's language deeply? What prevents you from taking the time to understand Allah's words properly?

Proving Karamat al-Awliya and the Four Types of Extraordinary Events
Nasafi explains the proof of karamat al-awliya and divides extraordinary events into four types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni proof for the miracles of saints (karamat al-awliya) and the classification of extraordinary events into four types: mu'jiza, karama, ma‘una, and ihana.

Core Idea
A saint's miracle proves the prophet's truth; extraordinary events are of four kinds.

The Mu'tazila denied miracles of saints to avoid confusion with prophethood. Sunni scholars affirmed them through transmitted reports and logical reasoning. This lesson examines their evidence and shows how karamat actually support prophethood. It also presents the fourfold division of extraordinary events.

Guided Path
1
Understand the debate
Read the passage to learn the Mu'tazila objection and the Sunni response. Note the key terms and the examples provided.
The text contrasts 'Ahl al-Haqq' with the Mu'tazila.
2
Analyze the proofs
Focus on the two examples: Asif bringing Bilqis's throne and 'Umar calling to Sariya. Understand how they serve as evidence for karamat.
3
Grasp the fourfold classification
The passage divides extraordinary events into four categories. Identify each category and its specific recipient.
The classification clarifies the purpose of each type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في إثبات كرامات الأولياء
يبين النسفي أن المعتزلة يمنعونها حتى لا يلتبس الأمر بالنبوة، ولأنه لا فائدة لها.
أما أهل الحق فيثبتونها ؛ لوجود أخبار كثيرة بذلك مثل صاحب سليمان، الذي أتى بعرش بلقيس قبل ارتداد الطرف، ومثل رؤية عمر لجيشه بنهاوند، وهو يقف على المنبر بالمدينة حتى قال يا سارية الجبل، وسمعه سارية.
وبعد أن يذكر أمثلة كثيرة لذلك يناقش كلام المعتزلة، ويبين أن الهوى هو الذي ساقهم إلى ما قالوا، فلو أمعنوا النظر لعلموا أن كرامة الولي هي معجزة للرسول، إذ هي دليل على صدق عقيدة الولي، وعقيدته هي ما جاء بها الرسول ثم يفرق بين المعجزة والكرامة، ويبين أن الناقض للعادة ينقسم إلى أربعة أقسام أ - معجزة: وهي خاصة بالرسول. ب - كرامة وهي خاصة بالأولياء. معونة : وهي خاصة للصالحين المؤمنين. د إهانة وتكون لمدَّعي الألوهية أو النبوة.
Discussion on proving the miracles of saints (karamat al-awliya). Al-Nasafi explains that the Mu'tazila prohibit them so that the matter is not confused with prophethood, and because there is no benefit in them. As for the People of Truth (Ahl al-Haqq), they affirm them due to the existence of many reports of that, such as the companion of Sulayman who brought the throne of Bilqis before the twinkling of an eye, and such as 'Umar's seeing his army at Nihawand while he was standing on the pulpit in Medina until he said, 'O Sariya, the mountain!' and Sariya heard him. After mentioning many examples of that, he discusses the speech of the Mu'tazila and shows that it is caprice that drove them to what they said. Had they pondered, they would have known that the saint's miracle (karama) is a miracle (mu'jiza) for the messenger, since it is evidence of the truthfulness of the saint's creed, and his creed is what the messenger brought. Then he distinguishes between miracle (mu'jiza) and saintly miracle (karama), and shows that the extraordinary event (al-naqid li'l-‘ada) is divided into four sections: A) Mu'jiza (miracle): specific to the messenger. B) Karama (saintly miracle): specific to the saints. C) Ma‘una (divine assistance): specific to righteous believers. D) Ihana (humiliation): for the claimant of divinity or prophethood.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on proving the miracles of saints (karamat al-awliya). It begins by stating the Mu'tazila's position: they deny karamat to avoid confusion with prophethood and because they see no benefit. Then the People of Truth (Ahl al-Haqq) affirm them based on multiple reports, such as the companion of Sulayman (likely Asif ibn Barkhiya) bringing the throne of Bilqis instantly, and the story of 'Umar on the minbar calling out to Sariya at Nihawand. After giving examples, the author argues that the Mu'tazila were driven by caprice; if they reflected, they would see that a saint's karama is actually a mu'jiza for the prophet, because it confirms the saint's true belief, which is derived from the prophet. Thus, there is no confusion. The passage then distinguishes between mu'jiza (prophetic miracle) and karama (saintly miracle), and further divides extraordinary events into four categories: (1) mu'jiza for prophets, (2) karama for saints, (3) ma‘una (divine assistance) for righteous believers, and (4) ihana (humiliation) for false claimants of divinity or prophethood. This classification clarifies the theological purpose of each type.

Key Terms
كرامة
معجزة
معونة
إهانة
ولي
ناقض للعادة
أهل الحق
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That karamat are identical to prophetic miracles and can cause confusion about prophethood.
Correction: The passage explains that karamat actually confirm the prophet's truth, so they do not cause confusion but rather strengthen belief in the prophet.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between a saint's karama and a prophet's mu'jiza?
A) They are completely unrelated.
B) The karama is a proof of the prophet's truth.
C) The karama is greater than the mu'jiza.
D) The karama is only for the saint's benefit.

Key Takeaway
Karama is a miracle for the saint and a proof for the prophet's truth; extraordinary events are of four types: prophetic miracles, saintly miracles, divine assistance, and humiliation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If a saint's miracle confirms the truth of the Prophet's message, how does that challenge you to re-evaluate your own connection to the Prophet ﷺ? What concrete step will you take today to strengthen that connection?
?
The Mu'tazila denied karamat out of caprice. Is there any belief you hold—about Allah, His prophets, or the unseen—that you cling to out of habit or pride rather than evidence? What would it cost you to submit to the truth?
?
The passage divides extraordinary events into four: mu'jiza, karama, ma'una, and ihana. Which of these do you most hope for in your life—and why? What does your answer reveal about the sincerity of your intention and your reliance on Allah?

Refuting the Mu'tazila Claim on Lam al-ʿĀqiba
Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila interpretation of lam as outcome by arguing it implies divine ignorance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that the Mu'tazila interpretation of the lam as outcome requires attributing ignorance to God, which is impossible.

Core Idea
God's perfect knowledge prevents Him from willing an outcome He knows will not occur.

Nasafi confronts a subtle hermeneutical claim by the Mu'tazila. They say the lam in verses like 'to worship Me' and 'to increase in sin' indicates outcome, not purpose. This would mean God's intention was not the actual result. Nasafi refutes this by a simple but powerful rational argument: such a usage only makes sense if the agent is ignorant of the outcome. Since God knows all, this interpretation is impossible. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overanalysis, then its translation. Let the flow of the argument sink in before diving into details.
Notice the contrast between 'lam al-ʿāqiba' and 'lam al-taʿlīl'.
2
Identify key terms
Focus on the terms 'lam al-ʿāqiba', 'lam al-taʿlīl', 'al-jahl bi-l-ʿawāqib' (ignorance of consequences), and 'al-safīh' (fool). Understand their meanings in context.
These terms are central to the refutation.
3
Analyze the logical argument
Trace Nasafi's reasoning: (a) Mu'tazila claim lam is for outcome, (b) using outcome only makes sense if agent is ignorant of true consequence, (c) God is not ignorant, (d) therefore the claim leads to attributing foolishness to God, which is impossible.
The argument is rational, not textual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقول : إن المعتزلة تزعم أن اللام في الآيتين لام العاقبة، لا لام التعليل ويرد قولهم هذا قائلا: إنما يتصور أن يريد أحد من أخر ما لا يكون منه أن لو كان الفاعل جاهلا بالعواقب، فأما من لم يجهل العواقب كيف يريد عاقبة لفعل يعلم حقيقته أنها لا تكون على ما يريد، وهل يفعل هذا إلا سفيه - تنزه الله عن ذلك و استعمال لام العاقبة فيمن يجوز عليه الجهل.
And he says: Indeed, the Mu'tazila claim that the lam in the two verses is the lam of outcome (lam al-ʿāqiba), not the lam of purpose (lam al-taʿlīl). And he refutes their statement, saying: One can only conceive that someone wills from another what will not be from him if the agent is ignorant of the consequences. But as for one who is not ignorant of the consequences, how can he will an outcome for an action of which he knows the true reality that it will not come about as he wills? And does anyone do this except a fool – exalted is Allah above that – and the use of lam al-ʿāqiba is only for one to whom ignorance is possible.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage addresses the Mu'tazila's hermeneutical move regarding the lam in the verses. The Mu'tazila claim that the lam in 'to worship Me' (liyaʿbudūn) and in 'to increase in sin' (liyazdādū) is lam al-ʿāqiba (indicating outcome) rather than lam al-taʿlīl (indicating purpose). This would mean God's intention was not the actual worship or increase of sin, but rather the outcome became those things. Al-Nasafi refutes this by a rational argument: such a usage (one intending an outcome that does not happen) only makes sense if the agent is ignorant of the true outcome. Since God knows all consequences perfectly, it is impossible for Him to will an outcome that He knows will not occur. Attributing such behavior to God would be foolish (sufah), which is impossible for Allah. Therefore, the lam must indicate purpose, confirming that God indeed willed the actions as described.

Key Terms
لام العاقبة
لام التعليل
الجهل بالعواقب
السفيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The lam al-ʿāqiba interpretation is a viable option that avoids attributing direct intent for evil to God.
Correction: Nasafi shows that this interpretation itself requires attributing ignorance to God, which is even more problematic, making it impossible.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi refute the Mu'tazila claim that the lam in the verses is lam al-ʿāqiba?
A) By citing consensus
B) By arguing that it would require God to be ignorant of the outcome, which is impossible
C) By saying the verses are unclear
D) By accepting it but reinterpreting

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila by showing that interpreting the lam as outcome necessitates attributing ignorance to God, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you interpret unexpected outcomes in your life, do you ever assume that Allah did not intend them—as if He were unaware of the result? How does Nasafi's argument about divine knowledge expose the error of such thinking, and how should it reshape your trust in Allah's purpose behind every decree?
?
The Mu'tazila's interpretation seemed linguistically plausible, yet led to a logical impossibility (ignorance). What plausible-sounding beliefs have you held that, if followed to their logical end, would imply something impossible about Allah? This week, commit to examining one such belief and replacing it with what the Qur'an and sound reason demand.
?
Nasafi calls the one who acts without knowledge a 'fool' (sufah). Have you ever acted in a way that assumed you knew better than Allah’s decree—perhaps by complaining about what He willed? Repent of that stance and resolve to embrace the purpose behind His commands, even when the outcome is hidden from you.

Interpreting 'I Did Not Create...' (51:56)
Nasafi offers two exegetical responses to a key verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite use of Quran 51:56 by presenting alternative interpretations that show the verse does not prove God wills only obedience.

Core Idea
The verse about worship does not prove that God wills only obedience.

The Mu'tazila cite Quran 51:56 to argue that God creates only for worship, implying He does not will unbelief. Nasafi counters by presenting two mainstream interpretations that show the verse is either general or has exceptions, thereby undermining their proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage for verse 51:56 and its translation. Note how Nasafi introduces the Mu'tazilite objection.
Pay attention to the two interpretations he mentions.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Locate the first interpretation: 'except to be servants to Me' (general, applies to all). Then the second: 'except for My command to worship' (which, even if conceded, has exceptions).
3
Understand the refutation
See how each interpretation removes the Mu'tazilite argument. The first makes the verse general, so it includes disbelievers. The second restricts the verse by excluding children and the insane, so it does not prove God wills only obedience.
4
Reflect on the key point
Consider why Nasafi argues that applying the verse generally is 'more appropriate' than restricting it. This shows the strength of the Sunni position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يرد على ما تعلقوا به من الآيات مثل قوله تعالى: وَمَا خَلَقْتُ الْجِنَّ وَالْإِنسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونَ [الذاريات: ٥٦] فيقول: إن كثيرا من أهل التأويل قالوا: معناه إلا ليكونوا عبادا لي، وهذا في الكافر والمؤمن، لا أن يقيدونه بفعلهم الاختياري، وهذا يجعل الآية جارية على العموم، وإجراؤها كذلك أولى من إجرائها على الخصوص، ومنهم من يقول: إلا لأمرهم بالعبادة، فلو حملت الآية على هذا لم يبق للخصم أي متعلق حتى ولو سلمنا أن المراد منها العبادة، إلا أنه خص منها الصغار، والمجانين لعدم التكليف، فيخص المتنازع وهم الكفرة، وتبقى الآية محمولة على من علم منهم الإيمان. وتعلقهم بقوله تعالى: يُرِيدُ اللَّهُ بِكُمُ الْيُسْرَ وَلَا يُرِيدُ بِكُمُ الْعُسْرَ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٥] وقولهم : إن الكفر أعسر العسر يجيب على ذلك أن هذا خطاب للمؤمنين بقوله يا أيها الذين أمنوا كتب عليكم الصيام. وتعلقهم بقوله تعالى: لَوْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ مَا أَشْرَكْنَا ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٤٨] وذلك على لسان المشركين. يقول النسفي : مراد الكفرة من ذكر المشيئة الأمر، لا حقيقة المشيئة.
He refutes what they cling to of the verses, such as His statement: 'And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me' (Quran 51:56). He says: Many of the people of interpretation said: Its meaning is except that they be servants to Me, and this applies to both disbeliever and believer, not that they restrict it to their voluntary action. This makes the verse general, and applying it generally is more appropriate than applying it specifically. And some of them say: Except for My command to them to worship. If the verse is interpreted in this way, then no argument remains for the opponent. Even if we concede that the intended meaning is worship, it is still specified by excluding children and the insane due to lack of obligation. Thus the disputants (the disbelievers) are specified, and the verse remains applicable to those of them known to have faith. And their clinging to His statement: 'God intends for you ease and does not intend for you hardship' (Quran 2:185). And their statement: Unbelief is the hardest of hardship. He answers that this is an address to believers in His saying: 'O you who have believed, fasting is prescribed for you.' And their clinging to His statement: 'If God had willed, we would not have associated partners' (Quran 6:148). And that is on the tongues of the polytheists. Al-Nasafi says: The intent of the disbelievers in mentioning the will is to command, not the reality of will.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage provides detailed exegesis. Nasafi first addresses the key verse 51:56 used by Mu'tazila. He notes two mainstream interpretations: (1) it means 'except to be servants to Me,' which applies to both believer and disbeliever without restricting to voluntary acts of worship, thus general; (2) it means 'except for My command to worship.' Under this interpretation, even if conceded, the verse is not absolute because children and the insane are excluded, so the verse can still be applied to those known to believe among the disbelievers. Then he addresses verse 2:185: Mu'tazila argue that God wills ease, and disbelief is the greatest hardship, so God cannot will disbelief. Nasafi responds that the verse is addressed specifically to believers in the context of fasting, not a general statement about all actions. Lastly, he addresses verse 6:148, where polytheists claim God willed if He had willed. Nasafi explains that this is a report of polytheists' speech, and their mention of 'will' means command, not actual will. Hence, these verses do not conflict with the position that God wills all things.

Key Terms
أهل التأويل
العموم
الخصوص
المكلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 51:56 proves that God creates all humans only for obedience, so He cannot will unbelief.
Correction: The verse can be interpreted generally (all are servants) or as a command with exceptions (children, insane), so it does not support the claim that God wills only obedience from every individual.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is one way scholars interpret the phrase 'except to worship Me' in Quran 51:56?
A) Except to obey My commands voluntarily
B) Except to be servants to Me, applying to both believer and disbeliever
C) Except to perform ritual prayers only
D) Except to acknowledge My existence

Key Takeaway
Nasafi shows that Quran 51:56 does not support Mu'tazilite determinism because it can be read as general or as a command with exceptions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read Quran 51:56, do you immediately assume it means God created you only to perform rituals of worship? Or do you consider the possibility that being a servant ('abd) of Allah encompasses every aspect of your life, including your struggles and failures? What would change in your daily awareness if you truly believed your very existence is an act of servanthood, regardless of your obedience at any moment?
?
Nasafi shows that even a verse that seems to support a wrong belief can be understood correctly through deeper interpretation. Think of a verse you have struggled with or misused. Are you willing to set aside your preconceived understanding and seek the interpretive tradition? What practical step will you take this week to deepen your understanding of a verse you've misunderstood?
?
The lesson reminds us that God's creation includes both believers and disbelievers, yet all are His servants in some sense. If servanthood is the purpose of creation, and you are already a servant by virtue of being created, what does that mean for your personal relationship with Allah? Are you content with being a servant who rebels, or will you strive to embody true submission? What one change will you make today to align your actions with your identity as His servant?

Refuting the Ease and Willing Verses (2:185, 6:148)
Nasafi refutes two additional verses using contextual and semantic analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes Mu'tazilite arguments from Quran 2:185 and 6:148 by showing they are context-specific or reports of disbelievers' speech.

Core Idea
Scriptural arguments must be understood in their proper context and audience.

The Mu'tazila also appeal to verses about God's will for ease and the polytheists' statement about God's will. Nasafi demonstrates that these verses are either addressed to a specific audience or are reports of disbelievers' speech, not affirmations of God's actual will, thus preserving the Sunni view that God wills all things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for both verses
Read the Arabic and translation for the sections on 2:185 and 6:148. Note the Mu'tazilite claims: ease for all, and polytheists' argument.
2
Understand Nasafi's response to the ease verse
Nasafi points out that 2:185 is addressed specifically to believers in the context of fasting, not a universal statement about God's will for all actions.
3
Understand Nasafi's response to the will verse
Nasafi explains that 6:148 is a report of the polytheists' speech; their mention of 'will' means command, not actual will.
4
Reflect on the broader principle
Consider how contextualizing verses is a key method in refuting scriptural objections. Nasafi does not deny the texts but reinterprets them within their proper scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يرد على ما تعلقوا به من الآيات مثل قوله تعالى: وَمَا خَلَقْتُ الْجِنَّ وَالْإِنسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونَ [الذاريات: ٥٦] فيقول: إن كثيرا من أهل التأويل قالوا: معناه إلا ليكونوا عبادا لي، وهذا في الكافر والمؤمن، لا أن يقيدونه بفعلهم الاختياري، وهذا يجعل الآية جارية على العموم، وإجراؤها كذلك أولى من إجرائها على الخصوص، ومنهم من يقول: إلا لأمرهم بالعبادة، فلو حملت الآية على هذا لم يبق للخصم أي متعلق حتى ولو سلمنا أن المراد منها العبادة، إلا أنه خص منها الصغار، والمجانين لعدم التكليف، فيخص المتنازع وهم الكفرة، وتبقى الآية محمولة على من علم منهم الإيمان. وتعلقهم بقوله تعالى: يُرِيدُ اللَّهُ بِكُمُ الْيُسْرَ وَلَا يُرِيدُ بِكُمُ الْعُسْرَ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٥] وقولهم : إن الكفر أعسر العسر يجيب على ذلك أن هذا خطاب للمؤمنين بقوله يا أيها الذين أمنوا كتب عليكم الصيام. وتعلقهم بقوله تعالى: لَوْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ مَا أَشْرَكْنَا ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٤٨] وذلك على لسان المشركين. يقول النسفي : مراد الكفرة من ذكر المشيئة الأمر، لا حقيقة المشيئة.
He refutes what they cling to of the verses, such as His statement: 'And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me' (Quran 51:56). He says: Many of the people of interpretation said: Its meaning is except that they be servants to Me, and this applies to both disbeliever and believer, not that they restrict it to their voluntary action. This makes the verse general, and applying it generally is more appropriate than applying it specifically. And some of them say: Except for My command to them to worship. If the verse is interpreted in this way, then no argument remains for the opponent. Even if we concede that the intended meaning is worship, it is still specified by excluding children and the insane due to lack of obligation. Thus the disputants (the disbelievers) are specified, and the verse remains applicable to those of them known to have faith. And their clinging to His statement: 'God intends for you ease and does not intend for you hardship' (Quran 2:185). And their statement: Unbelief is the hardest of hardship. He answers that this is an address to believers in His saying: 'O you who have believed, fasting is prescribed for you.' And their clinging to His statement: 'If God had willed, we would not have associated partners' (Quran 6:148). And that is on the tongues of the polytheists. Al-Nasafi says: The intent of the disbelievers in mentioning the will is to command, not the reality of will.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage provides detailed exegesis. Nasafi first addresses the key verse 51:56 used by Mu'tazila. He notes two mainstream interpretations: (1) it means 'except to be servants to Me,' which applies to both believer and disbeliever without restricting to voluntary acts of worship, thus general; (2) it means 'except for My command to worship.' Under this interpretation, even if conceded, the verse is not absolute because children and the insane are excluded, so the verse can still be applied to those known to believe among the disbelievers. Then he addresses verse 2:185: Mu'tazila argue that God wills ease, and disbelief is the greatest hardship, so God cannot will disbelief. Nasafi responds that the verse is addressed specifically to believers in the context of fasting, not a general statement about all actions. Lastly, he addresses verse 6:148, where polytheists claim God willed if He had willed. Nasafi explains that this is a report of polytheists' speech, and their mention of 'will' means command, not actual will. Hence, these verses do not conflict with the position that God wills all things.

Key Terms
المشركون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse about ease (2:185) implies God cannot will any hardship, such as unbelief.
Correction: The verse is addressed specifically to believers regarding fasting, not a universal statement about God's will for all actions.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi respond to the Mu'tazilite claim that verse 2:185 ('God intends ease') proves God cannot will unbelief?
A) He says the verse is abrogated
B) He says the verse is addressed specifically to believers about fasting
C) He says the verse is metaphorical
D) He says the verse is unclear

Key Takeaway
Nasafi shows that verses 2:185 and 6:148 do not contradict God's universal will when understood in their specific contexts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used a verse from the Quran out of its original context to justify a position that suits your desires? How can you train yourself to first ask 'Who is being addressed?' before applying a verse to your life?
?
The polytheists in 6:148 blamed God's will for their shirk. In what areas of your life do you subtly blame circumstances or God's decree for your own negligence? Take one specific area today and commit to acting without excuses.
?
When you read 'God intends ease for you' (2:185), do you assume it means every path will be easy? Reflect on a time when obedience to God required hardship. Did you still believe that God intended ease for you? How does that tension shape your trust in Him?

Evidence for Punishment in the Grave
Nasafi proves punishment in the grave using Quranic verse and prophetic hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran and hadith establish the reality of punishment in the grave according to the majority of the Ummah.

Core Idea
Scripture proves grave punishment: the Quran and sound hadith override doubts.

This lesson examines the scriptural basis for the doctrine of punishment in the grave (ʿadhāb al-qabr). Nasafi cites a Quranic verse showing the people of Pharaoh undergo punishment before resurrection, and a prophetic hadith linking common negligence to grave punishment. These texts form the primary evidence for this belief among Ahl al-Sunna.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how Nasafi begins by stating the consensus and then presents two distinct proofs.
The passage is short but packed with key evidence.
2
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Focus on the verse from Surah Ghafir (40:46). Nasafi argues that the exposure to the Fire 'morning and evening' occurs before the Day of Resurrection, so it must happen in the grave. Consider why this is a strong proof.
This is the primary textual evidence from the Quran.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the hadith warning about urine. Note that Nasafi lists multiple narrators to confirm its authenticity. Understand how a practical hygiene instruction points to a major cause of punishment in the grave.
This hadith is categorized as sound (ṣaḥīḥ) by scholars.
4
Understand ‘inferential knowledge’
Nasafi says these reports produce ‘inferential knowledge’ (al-ʿilm al-istidlālī). Reflect on what this means: the evidence is strong but not necessarily certain; it is derived through reasoning from scripture.
This concept distinguishes kalam from pure belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في إثبات عذاب القبر
أثبت جمهور الأمة عذاب القبر لورود السمع بذلك حيث قال الله تعالى: ﴿ النَّارُ يُعْرَضُونَ عَلَيْهَا غُدُوًّا وَعَشِيًّا وَيَوْمَ تَقُومُ السَّاعَةُ أَدْخِلُوا آلَ فِرْعَوْنَ أَشَدَّ الْعَذَابِ ﴾ [غافر: ٤٦] ولا يكون العذاب قبل القيامة إلا في القبر، وقد وردت أخبار كثيرة في هذا توجب العلم الاستدلالي من ذلك قوله عليه السلام: "استنزهوا من البول فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه" وهو حديث صحيح ذكره الحاكم في المستدرك، وابن ماجه في والإمام أحمد في مسنده، ورواه الدارقطني من حديث أبي هريرة، والشوكاني في نيل الأوطار جـ ۱ ص ۸۲ من حديث أنس بلفظ "تنزهوا".
The discussion on establishing the punishment of the grave.
The majority of the Ummah affirmed the punishment of the grave because of the scriptural evidence that came concerning that, where Allah Almighty said: 'The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening, and on the Day when the Hour will be established: "Admit the family of Pharaoh to the severest punishment."' (Ghafir 46). And there is no punishment before the Resurrection except in the grave. And many reports have come concerning this that necessitate inferential knowledge, among them his statement, peace be upon him: 'Guard yourselves from urine, for indeed the majority of the punishment of the grave is from it.' And it is a sound hadith mentioned by al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak, and Ibn Majah, and Imam Ahmad in his Musnad, and al-Daraqutni narrated it from the hadith of Abu Huraira, and al-Shawkani in Nayl al-Awtar, vol. 1 p. 82 from the hadith of Anas with the wording 'Guard yourselves.'
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage argues for the reality of punishment in the grave (adhab al-qabr), a doctrine held by the majority of the Ummah (Ahl al-Sunna). The proof is from scripture (sam'): first, a Quranic verse (Ghafir 46) which states that the people of Pharaoh are exposed to the Fire morning and evening before the Day of Judgment; since this exposure occurs before the Resurrection, it must take place in the grave. Second, multiple hadiths, including a sound one warning against urine because it is a major cause of grave punishment. Nasafi notes that these reports produce 'inferential knowledge' (al-‘ilm al-istidlalī), meaning that while not necessarily yielding certainty, they provide strong probable knowledge through cumulative evidence. The passage includes a list of narrators to establish the hadith's authenticity.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
السمع
العلم الاستدلالي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The punishment of the grave is not mentioned in the Quran.
Correction: Nasafi shows that the Quran does mention it implicitly in Surah Ghafir 46, where the people of Pharaoh are punished before the Resurrection, and such punishment can only be in the grave.

Checkpoint
What Quranic verse does Nasafi use as evidence for punishment in the grave?
A) Surah Ghafir 46
B) Surah Yasin 51
C) Surah Al-Fatiha 1
D) Surah Al-Ikhlas 1

Key Takeaway
Nasafi establishes punishment in the grave through scriptural evidence from the Quran and hadith, producing inferential knowledge that grounds this article of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that the Prophet ﷺ warned that a major cause of grave punishment is negligence regarding urine. When you use the toilet, do you truly guard yourself against urine splashes, or do you dismiss this as trivial? How will you change your practice starting today?
?
The verse about Pharaoh's people exposes them to fire morning and evening. If you were to die tonight, what would your 'morning and evening' be? Are you living in a way that prepares you for that reality, or are you ignoring it?
?
Nasafi says these reports produce inferential knowledge—strong enough to base your faith on. Do you actually believe in the punishment of the grave with certainty? If not, what is holding you back from fully embracing what the Quran and authentic hadith have taught?

Proof for the Punishment of the Grave
Nasafi proves the reality of grave punishment via hadith and Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and textual proofs for the punishment and bliss of the grave according to Nasafi and the Maturidi school.

Core Idea
The dead experience pain or pleasure through a soul that remains conscious in a sleep-like state.

This lesson examines the classical proof for ‘adhāb al-qabr, affirming that Allah can grant the deceased a form of life to experience reward or punishment. Nasafi cites a key hadith with ʿUmar and the Prophet’s reply, alongside Quranic verses on martyrs, to establish that the soul persists after bodily death.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source passage once, then its literal translation. Notice the structure: denial, possibility, evidence.
The passage includes both the author's and commentator's views.
2
Identify the two proofs
Look for the hadith of ʿUmar and the Quranic verses (Āl ʿImrān 169 and al-Baqarah 154). These are the primary textual evidences.
The hadith shows the dead are given intellect to feel.
3
Understand the condition of life
Note that Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi require a kind of life for sensation. This is supported by the Quranic verses about martyrs being alive.
This life is not full bodily life but a barzakh state.
4
Reflect on the commentator’s analogy
The commentator compares the soul after death to a sleeping person: feeling occurs but is not perceived by others.
This explains how punishment can occur without full bodily life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن النسفي يذكر أن بعض المعتزلة والجمهية ينكرون عذاب القبر، ولأمانة البحث فإني لم أجد للمعتزلة والجهمية إنكارا لذلك، وقد بينت ذلك في موضعه من التحقيق مستشهدا بأقوالهم. والنسفي كأي باحث كلامي منصف يعتبر عذاب القبر من الأمور الممكنة فلله تعالى أن يعيد للميت نوعا من الحياة مقدار ما يتألم أو يتلذذ أما أنا فأحسب أن الذي يموت هو الجسد أما الروح فإنها تكون في فترة شبيهة بالنوم بحيث تحس بكل شيء يأتي من الله مثل ما يحدث تماما بالنسبة للنائم حيث يعايش النائم في الحلم أشياء كثيرة لا يحسها من يجاوره في اليقظة. ولا يعني هذا أن جسد الميت لا يحس بالألم أو اللذة وإنما يعني أن تأثير الروح وسيطرتها على الجسد أصبح أقل مما كان في دنيا الناس. لنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: والنسفي يستدل على وجود عذاب القبر أو نعيمه بقول سيدنا عمر للنبي أو يكون معي عقلي؟ وقول الرسول عليه السلام له: 'نعم' دليل على ما يحدث في القبر وهو دليل أيضا على أن الميت يعطي نوعا من الحياة. ثم يذكر النسفي أن أبا الحسن الرستغفني وأبا منصور الماتريدي اشترطا وجود نوع من الحياة ليحس بها الميت التعذيب أو الالتذاذ ثم يستدل لقولهما بقوله تعالى : ( وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ الَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَان بَلْ أَحْيَاءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ ) [آل عمران: ١٦٩] وبقوله سبحانه: وَلَا نَقُولُوا لِمَن يُقْتَلُ في سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَاتٌ بَلْ أَحْيَاءٌ وَلَكِن لَا تَشْعُرُونَ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٥٤].
Then al-Nasafi mentions that some of the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya deny the punishment of the grave. For the sake of research integrity, I have not found for the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya a denial of that, and I have explained that in its place in the investigation citing their statements. Al-Nasafi, like any fair theological researcher, considers the punishment of the grave to be among possible matters. For Allah is able to restore to the dead a kind of life to the extent that he feels pain or pleasure. As for me, I think that what dies is the body, while the soul is in a period similar to sleep, such that it feels everything that comes from Allah, exactly like what happens to a sleeper, who experiences many things in a dream that others next to him do not feel while awake. This does not mean that the body of the dead does not feel pain or pleasure, but rather that the soul's influence and control over the body has become less than it was in the world of people. The Prophet: Al-Nasafi uses as evidence for the existence of the punishment or bliss of the grave the saying of our master Umar to the Prophet: 'Or will my intellect be with me?' and the saying of the Messenger to him: 'Yes' is evidence for what happens in the grave, and it is also evidence that the dead is given a kind of life. Then al-Nasafi mentions that Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi required the existence of a kind of life so that the dead can feel punishment or pleasure. Then he uses as evidence for their statement the saying of Allah: 'And do not think that those who are killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather, they are alive with their Lord, receiving provision' [Al-Imran 169] and His saying: 'And do not say of those who are killed in the way of Allah, 'They are dead.' Rather, they are alive, but you do not perceive' [Al-Baqarah 154].
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the reality of the punishment and bliss of the grave. It begins by noting that some Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya deny it, but the author (possibly the commentator) states he has not found such denial from them. Then al-Nasafi is described as a fair scholar who considers grave punishment possible. The commentator adds his own view: the body dies, but the soul persists in a sleep-like state, able to feel what Allah sends, though its influence on the body is diminished. The proof from hadith: Umar asked the Prophet if he would have his intellect with him in the grave, and the Prophet answered 'yes', indicating the dead are given a kind of life to experience reward or punishment. Then, al-Nasafi cites Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi who require some form of life for sensation, supporting this with Quranic verses about martyrs being alive with their Lord and the general statement that those killed in Allah's way are alive though people do not perceive it.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
الروح
الجسد
الحياة البرزخية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the soul is completely inactive after death, having no awareness or sensation.
Correction: This passage shows that the soul remains in a sleep-like state, able to feel pain or pleasure from Allah, and the dead are given a kind of life to experience punishment or bliss.

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence al-Nasafi uses from hadith to prove the punishment of the grave?
A) The hadith of Umar asking about his intellect being with him, and the Prophet replying 'Yes'
B) The Quranic verse about martyrs being alive
C) The consensus of the companions
D) The statement of Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
The punishment and bliss of the grave are real because Allah grants the dead a form of life through which they experience reward or punishment, as evidenced by hadith and Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that the soul after death feels everything like in a dream, but even more real. What dream have you had that felt so real it changed your waking actions? If the barzakh is like that but with the actual consequences of your deeds, how are you preparing for that waking reality?
?
Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) was so certain of the unseen that his first question to the Prophet about the grave was about his intellect. Are you using your intellect now to seek certainty about what comes after death, or are you distracted by what you can see? What would you ask the Prophet if you could meet him today?
?
The passage says the soul's control over the body becomes less after death, but the sensation of pain or pleasure remains. If your soul were separated from your body tonight, what would it feel because of what you did today? Write down one habit you will change starting now so that your barzakh begins with bliss, not regret.

The Proof of Intercession for Major Sinners
Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila on intercession using hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi proves the permissibility of intercession for grave sinners and refutes the Mu'tazila objections.

Core Idea
Prophetic intercession is specifically for the major sinners of the Muslim community.

This passage tackles a critical point of difference between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila: whether intercession (shafa'a) can benefit grave sinners. Nasafi first presents the Sunni premise that Allah can forgive major sins, then counters the Mu'tazila arguments using explicit hadiths. The lesson shows how scriptural evidence and logical consistency defend the doctrine of intercession.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Sunni position
Notice how Nasafi starts with the Sunni premise: 'Since it is possible for Allah to forgive a major sinner, it is possible for Him to accept intercession.' This establishes the logical basis.
The possibility of forgiveness is the key foundation.
2
Learn the Mu'tazila arguments
Identify the three proofs the Mu'tazila bring: Quran 40:18, the claim that intercession is only for the obedient, and the argument that it encourages sin.
Each proof relies on their view that grave sinners are eternally punished.
3
See the refutation through hadith
Nasafi directly quotes the Prophet's statement 'My intercession is for the people of major sins' and interprets the Mu'tazila proof texts as referring to those who deem sin permissible (mustahill).
The hadith 'Whoever says La ilaha illa Allah will enter Paradise even if he commits adultery and theft' reinforces the point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في إثبات الشفاعة. لما جاز أن يغفر الله لمرتكب الكبيرة على رأي أهل السنة، جاز له سبحانه أن يقبل الشفاعة من الرسل الأطهار والآباء وغيرهم. ويذكر النسفي رأي المعتزلة بامتناعها، وذلك بناء على رأيهم في صاحب الكبيرة ويقدم أدلتهم منها قوله تعالى: ﴿ مَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعٍ يُطَاعُ ﴾ [غافر: 18] فمرتكب الكبيرة ظالم، والله تعالى لا يحب من أبغضه، والشفاعة تكون للمطيع لا للعاصي - كما أن الشفاعة لأهل الكبائر تجرئة للناس على الذنوب. ثم يبدأ في مناقشتهم ليبطل أقوالهم، مستدلا بقول الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم: "شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر في أمتي" والحديث صحيح رواه ابن ماجه في سننه من حديث جابر ج 1441 ورواه الحاكم في المستدرك من حديث أنس مالك بن ج 1 ص 69. ويقول: إن ما استدل به المعتزلة والخوارج من الأحاديث إنما يحمل على المستحل ويدعم كلامه بما روي عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: "من قال لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة وإن زنى وإن سرق" والحديث صحيح رواه مسلم من حديث أبي ذر ج 2 ص 94.
Discussion on establishing intercession. Since it is possible for Allah to forgive the committer of a major sin according to the view of Ahl al-Sunna, it is possible for Him, exalted, to accept intercession from the noble messengers, fathers, and others. And Nasafi mentions the opinion of the Mu'tazila that it is impossible, and that is based on their view regarding the committer of a major sin. He presents their proofs, among them His statement, the Most High: 'For the wrongdoers there is no friend nor any intercessor to be obeyed' [Ghafir: 18]. So the committer of a major sin is a wrongdoer, and Allah does not love one whom He has detested, and intercession is for the obedient, not for the disobedient – also, intercession for the people of major sins would embolden people to commit sins. Then he begins to discuss with them to invalidate their statements, adducing the saying of the Messenger, peace be upon him: 'My intercession is for the people of major sins in my community' – and the hadith is authentic, recorded by Ibn Majah in his Sunan from the hadith of Jabir (vol. 1441) and by al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak from the hadith of Anas ibn Malik (vol. 1, p. 69). And he says: What the Mu'tazila and Khawarij used as evidence from the hadiths is only to be interpreted as pertaining to the one who deems (sin) permissible. And he supports his statement with what was narrated from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Whoever says "There is no god but Allah" will enter Paradise, even if he commits adultery and even if he steals' – and the hadith is authentic, recorded by Muslim from the hadith of Abu Dharr (vol. 2, p. 94).
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage addresses the doctrine of intercession (shafa'a) for grave sinners. Nasafi first states the Ahl al-Sunna position: because God can forgive major sins, He can accept intercession from prophets and others. He then presents the Mu'tazila view that intercession is impossible for grave sinners, based on their own earlier position. Their proofs include Quran 40:18 which denies intercession for wrongdoers, and the reasoning that a grave sinner is a wrongdoer, that God does not love such a person, that intercession is only for the obedient, and that allowing intercession would encourage sin. Nasafi then refutes them using a prophetic hadith explicitly stating that his intercession is for the people of major sins. He argues that the Qur'anic verses and hadiths cited by the Mu'tazila and Khawarij actually refer to the one who deems sin permissible (mustahill), not the general sinner. He supports this with another hadith that whoever says 'La ilaha illa Allah' enters Paradise even if he commits major sins like adultery and theft.

Key Terms
الشفاعة
مرتكب الكبيرة
المعتزلة
أهل السنة
المستحل
الخوارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intercession is only for the obedient, and grave sinners have no hope of intercession.
Correction: Nasafi shows that the Prophet explicitly said his intercession is for the people of major sins, and that verses about 'wrongdoers' refer to those who deem sin permissible.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi refute the Mu'tazila argument that Quran 40:18 denies intercession for wrongdoers?
A) He argues that the verse applies only to the mustahill (one who deems sin permissible).
B) He says the verse was abrogated.
C) He claims intercession is only for the obedient.
D) He denies that grave sinners are wrongdoers.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's explicit hadith establishes that his intercession is specifically for the major sinners of his community, refuting Mu'tazila objections.

The Necessity of Khabar for Knowledge: Mutawatir and Prophetic Reports
Imam Nasafi defines the conditions for reports that produce certain knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why only reports that are immune to falsehood—specifically mutawatir and prophetic reports—can produce certain knowledge, and how this relates to the role of khabar in human speech.

Core Idea
Only reports that cannot be false yield certain knowledge.

Imam Nasafi begins by illustrating the fundamental role of informative speech (khabar) in all human communication. Without the capacity to convey information, speech loses its purpose, and humans are reduced to beasts. He then addresses the claim that reports can be true or false, asserting that only reports immune to falsehood produce knowledge. This sets the stage for identifying the two types of reports that qualify: mutawatir and those supported by miraculous proof.

Guided Path
1
Understand the role of khabar in speech
Read the opening illustration about how prohibitions, vocatives, and wishes all contain an implicit informative component. Consider why Nasafi argues that without this, speech would be meaningless.
This shows the centrality of khabar to all communication.
2
Identify the criterion for knowledge-yielding reports
Notice the objection that reports can be true or false. Then focus on Nasafi's response: 'ما يحتمل الكذب لا يوجب العلم' (what admits falsehood does not necessitate knowledge). This is the key principle.
3
Learn the two types of certain reports
Identify the two categories: (1) mutawatir reports, where a lie is inconceivable, and (2) reports supported by miraculous proof (burhan mu'jizi), i.e., prophetic statements. Understand why each is immune to falsehood.
These are the only sources of certain knowledge from reports.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this distinction matters for Islamic epistemology and theology. How does it ground reliance on transmitted religious knowledge?
This connects to the broader field of samiyyat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تضربني ) (1) وكذا فيه إخبار عن قبح المنهي عنه، ولولا هو لخرج النهي من أن يكون صادرا عن حكيم وإذا قال: يا زيد فكأنه قال : أدعوا زيدا، وإذا قال: ليت زيدا عندنا فكأنه قال : أتمنى كون زيد عندنا، وإذا كان كذلك علم أن الكلام كله يبطل ببطلان الخبر وتتعطل فائدة السمع واللسان، ويلتحق الإنسان بالبهائم. وما يقولون: إن الخبر يتنوع إلى صدق وكذب، نقول : ما يحتمل الكذب لا يوجب العلم. الخبر الموجب للعلم] وإنما يوجب العلم ما لا يتصور كونه كذبا (3)، وهو ما تواتر من الأخبار، إذ كون مثله كذبا مستحيل (4) وكذا ما تأيد بالبرهان المعجزي، وهو قول الرسول عليه السلام، وقط لم يتمكن كذب في هذين الخبرين، والله الموفق(6).
It beats me? (1) And likewise in it there is information about the ugliness of the forbidden thing, and were it not for that, the prohibition would cease to be issued from a wise one. And when he says: O Zaid, it is as if he says: I call Zaid. And when he says: If only Zaid were with us, it is as if he says: I wish Zaid were with us. And when it is so, it is known that all speech is invalidated by the invalidation of the report (khabar), and the benefit of hearing and tongue becomes void, and man joins the beasts. And what they say: the report is divided into truth and falsehood, we say: what admits falsehood does not necessitate knowledge. The report that necessitates knowledge: only what cannot be conceived as false necessitates knowledge (3), and that is the mutawatir (widespread) reports, since the likeness of it being false is impossible (4), and likewise what is supported by miraculous proof, and that is the statement of the Messenger, peace be upon him, and absolutely no falsehood can occur in these two reports, and God is the granter of success (6).
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage defines the type of report (khabar) that yields certain knowledge. It begins by illustrating the importance of khabar in speech: if there were no informative content in a prohibition, the prohibition would not come from a wise being. Similarly, vocatives and wishes imply informative content. Therefore, if khabar is invalidated, all speech becomes useless. The author then addresses the claim that reports can be true or false. He responds that what can be false does not yield knowledge. The only reports that yield knowledge are those that cannot be false. These are of two types: (1) mutawatir reports, where it is impossible for such a large number to agree on a lie, and (2) reports supported by miraculous proof (burhan mu'jizi), i.e., the statements of prophets. In these two types, falsehood cannot occur. Thus, the author establishes the epistemic value of reliable transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All reports, including those that might be false, can produce certain knowledge.
Correction: Nasafi explicitly states that 'what admits falsehood does not necessitate knowledge' (ما يحتمل الكذب لا يوجب العلم). Only reports immune to falsehood (mutawatir and prophetic) yield knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of report does NOT yield certain knowledge?
A) Mutawatir reports
B) Prophetic reports supported by miracles
C) Reports that can be false
D) Reports that are true

Key Takeaway
Only mutawatir reports and prophetic reports supported by miracles can give us certain knowledge because they are immune to falsehood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a religious claim, do you check whether it is mutawatir or supported by a miracle? Or do you accept it because it sounds familiar? What would change in your life if you only built your faith on certain knowledge?
?
If all speech depends on the reality of khabar, have you ever considered that your own words carry the weight of truth? Are you careful to only report what you are certain of, especially about Allah and His messenger?
?
The Prophet's statement is protected from falsehood by divine proof. Do you treat his words as if they are more certain than your own opinions? What would it look like to submit to a prophetic command you find difficult, knowing it is backed by absolute knowledge?

Refuting the Mu'tazila on Divine Knowledge and Testing
Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila misinterpretation of verses about testing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Quranic verses about testing do not imply Allah acquires new knowledge, but rather manifest His eternal and unchanging knowledge.

Core Idea
Allah's testing reveals His eternal knowledge, not new information.

The Mu'tazila argued that certain Quranic verses, such as 'that We may know who follows the Messenger', suggest Allah gains knowledge through events. Imam Nasafi refutes this by clarifying that such expressions are about manifestation, not acquisition. This passage from Tabsirat al-Adilla shows how to correctly interpret these verses within Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to understand the flow.
Note the author's confident tone at the beginning.
2
Understand the initial argument
Notice how the author points out that if the Mu'tazila admit non-existent things are known, they contradict their own position.
This sets up the refutation.
3
Analyze the reinterpretation of verses
See how the author reinterprets 'li-na'lama' and similar phrases as manifesting what was already known in eternity.
Each verse is explained similarly.
4
Examine the treatment of 'la'alla'
Understand that 'perhaps' when attributed to Allah indicates certainty or is used for encouraging others.
This clarifies another potential misinterpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قالوا كل ذلك كان معدوما. فقد أقروا بكون المعدوم معلوما، وتركوا مذهبهم. وهذا مذهب يفنى العلم به عن الإطالة في رده وإبطاله. والله الموفق. ولا تعلق لهم بما تعلقوا به من الآيات، فإن الابتلاء من الله تعالى ليس ليثبت له به العلم كما في حق من يجوز عليه الجهل بالعواقب، بل الابتلاء منه تعالى ليظهر ما علم في الأزل على ما علم به. وكذا قوله تعالى: لِنَعْلَمَ مَن يَتَّبِعُ الرَّسُولَ لنعلم كائنا ما قد علم أنه يكون ولنعلم موجودا ما قد علم أنه يوجد، وكذا قوله: لِنَعْلَمَ أَيُّ الْحِزْبَيْنِ ليظهر ما كنا علمناه على ما علمناه، وقوله تعالى: لِنَنظُرَ كَيْفَ تَعْمَلُونَ أي ليظهر علمكم على ما كان علم، والله الموفق. وكلمة "لعل" من الله واجبة، فكان ذلك إخبارا على القطع لا على الترجي، أو ذكر ذلك لترجية غيره ليفعل ذلك الفعل على رجاء منه أن يحصل المقصود والله أعلم. ولأرباب التأويل في تأويل هذه الآيات كلام طويل فمن أراد الزيادة على ما بينا فعليه الرجوع إلى تصانيفهم، فأما كتابنا هذا فلا يحتمل الاستقصاء في شرح ذلك. وبالله العصمة.
And if they say that all that was non-existent, then they have admitted that the non-existent is known, and they have abandoned their doctrine. This is a doctrine that knowledge itself suffices to refute and invalidate without lengthy reply. And Allah is the giver of success. They have no support from the verses they cling to, for testing (al-ibtila') from Allah is not to establish knowledge for Him, as in the case of one for whom ignorance of consequences is possible; rather, testing from Him is to manifest what He knew in eternity according to how He knew it. Similarly, His saying: 'That We may know who follows the Messenger' (means) to know that which He already knew would occur, and to know as existing what He already knew would exist. Similarly, His saying: 'That We may know which of the two parties' (means) to manifest what We knew according to how We knew it. And His saying: 'That We may see how you act' (means) to manifest your action according to what He knew. And Allah is the giver of success. And the word 'la'alla' from Allah is obligatory (wajiba); thus it is a statement of certainty, not of hope. Or it is mentioned to give hope to others so that they perform that action hoping that the objective will be achieved. And Allah knows best. The people of interpretation (arbab al-ta'wil) have much to say regarding the interpretation of these verses; whoever desires more than what we have explained should refer to their works, for this book of ours cannot accommodate exhaustive explanation of that. And with Allah is protection.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Mu'tazila argument based on certain Quranic verses. The author begins by noting that if the Mu'tazila say all future events were non-existent, they have admitted that the non-existent is known to Allah, thus contradicting their own position. He then dismisses their view as so weak that knowledge itself renders lengthy refutation unnecessary. Next, he addresses their proof from verses like 'li-na'lama' (that We may know). The author explains that testing (ibtila') from Allah is not to acquire knowledge, as He is not subject to ignorance; rather, it is to manifest what He has always known in eternity. He interprets each verse: 'li-na'lama man yattabi'u al-rasul' means to manifest the already known event; 'li-na'lama ayyu al-hizbayn' means to manifest what was already known; 'li-nanzura kayfa ta'malun' means to manifest your deeds according to His prior knowledge. Finally, he discusses the word 'la'alla' (perhaps) when attributed to Allah: it indicates certainty (qat') not possibility, or it is used to give hope to others. He concludes by stating that those who desire more detail should consult other works, as this book cannot provide exhaustive treatment.

لعل
العلم
الأزل
التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Verses like 'li-na'lama' show that Allah learns new things from events.
Correction: The author explains that these verses are meant to manifest what Allah already knows eternally; testing does not add to His knowledge.

Checkpoint

A) To acquire new knowledge of their actions
B) To manifest what He already knew in eternity
C) To change His prior decree
D) To see how they act for the first time

Key Takeaway
Allah's knowledge is eternal and unchanging; Quranic verses about testing merely manifest what He already knows.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself thinking that your actions or prayers are noticed by Allah as if He is learning something new? This lesson teaches that His knowledge is eternal. How does that change the way you approach your deeds? Write one specific action you will perform today with the conviction that Allah already knows it and still values it.
?
When you read verses like 'that We may see how you act', do you truly believe that your actions are already known to Allah before you do them? If yes, how does that impact your sincerity and your struggle against hypocrisy? Commit to one act of worship today done solely for His sight, knowing He already knows what will happen.
?
The Mu'tazila thought Allah's knowledge was limited to what exists. Have you ever subtly doubted that Allah knows your deepest struggles before they happen? Repent from any imperfect belief, and in your next prayer, thank Allah for knowing you completely before you even exist.

The Mu'tazila's Transmitted Proofs for the Createdness of the Quran
The Mu'tazila present two Quranic proofs for the createdness of the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's Quranic arguments for the createdness of the Quran, specifically their interpretation of the terms 'ja'l' and 'muhdath'.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila argue that the Quran is created because it is 'made' and 'newly revealed'.

The Mu'tazila, a theological school, used Quranic verses to support their claim that the Quran is created. In this passage, they cite two key arguments: one based on the word 'ja'l' (making) and another based on the description of revelation as 'muhdath' (newly revealed). Let's examine their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila's transmitted proofs
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the two verses they cite.
2
Analyze the first proof: ja'l = khalq
Examine how the Mu'tazila equate 'making' with 'creating' from the verse 'We have made it an Arabic Quran'. Consider whether this equation is valid.
This is a key point of contention with Sunni scholars.
3
Analyze the second proof: muhdath = makhluq
Look at the verses that describe the 'reminder' as 'muhdath'. The Mu'tazila claim 'muhdath' is synonymous with 'makhluq'. Think about the implications.
The Sunni response distinguishes between 'muhdath' in time and 'created'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأدلة النقلية للمعتزلة على أن القرآن محدث. واحتجت المعتزلة بقوله تعالى: إنا جعلناه قرآنا عربيا والجعل والتخليق واحد. وبقوله: ﴿ ما يأتيهم من ذكر من ربهم محدث ﴾، ﴿ وما يأتيهم من ذكر من الرحمن محدث ﴾ وهذا نص إذ لا فرق بين المحدث والمخلوق.
The transmitted proofs of the Mu'tazila that the Quran is created. The Mu'tazila argued by His saying: 'Indeed, We have made it an Arabic Quran' and making and creating are one. And by His saying: 'No reminder comes to them from their Lord but it is newly revealed (muhdath)' and 'No reminder comes to them from the Most Merciful but it is newly revealed (muhdath).' This is explicit, for there is no difference between the newly revealed (muhdath) and the created (makhluq).
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazila's transmitted arguments from the Quran for the createdness of the Quran. They cite two verses: first, 'Indeed, We have made it an Arabic Quran' (Surah az-Zukhruf, 43:3), arguing that the word 'making' (ja'l) is synonymous with 'creating' (khalq), implying the Quran is created. Second, they cite two verses that describe the 'reminder' (dhikr) coming from Allah as 'muhdath' (newly revealed), and they claim there is no difference between 'muhdath' and 'makhluq' (created). Thus, they conclude the Quran is a created entity.

Key Terms
محدث (muhdath)
مخلوق (makhluq)
جعل (ja'l)
تخليق (takhlīq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'ja'l' in the Quran always means 'khalq' (creation ex nihilo).
Correction: In Sunni theology, 'ja'l' can mean to make or appoint, not necessarily create from nothing. The Mu'tazila's equation is disputed.

Checkpoint

A) The Quran is created because 'ja'l' means 'khalq'.
B) The Quran is eternal because it is Arabic.
C) The Quran is uncreated because it is from Allah.
D) The Quran is a miracle.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila use Quranic verses to argue that the Quran is created by equating 'making' with 'creating' and 'newly revealed' with 'created'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Commit to reciting the next verse with the awareness that it is not a created thing but the very words of Allah.
?
If the Quran were truly created, then what would that imply about Allah's attribute of speech? Does He still speak? This lesson forces you to consider: is your faith based on a temporal book or an eternal attribute of Allah? How would your relationship with the Quran change if you believed it to be created? Ask Allah to make you among those who cherish His speech as eternal.
?
The Mu'tazila used these verses to argue for creation. Have you ever felt a tension between the apparent meaning of 'made' and 'newly revealed' and the belief that the Quran is uncreated? How do you reconcile them? This is a test of your trust in the understanding of the Salaf. Resolve to seek deeper knowledge and not rely on superficial readings.

Refuting the Literal Speech of Jinn through Epileptics
Nasafi refutes the argument that jinn literally speak through epileptics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's rational and hadith-based refutation of the claim that jinn literally speak through epileptics, and how he establishes metaphorical attribution.

Core Idea
Speech attributed to jinn is metaphorical, not literal.

Nasafi addresses a common objection from those who claim that the speech of an epileptic is actually the speech of a jinn. He begins by dismissing this argument as lacking authority, then provides a rational proof and an analogy from the hadith of the angel speaking on Umar's tongue. This lesson unpacks his refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the overall flow of Nasafi's argument.
Notice how Nasafi first dismisses the claim then provides two arguments.
2
Identify the two arguments
Find the rational argument (the epileptic's tongue is not under the jinn's power) and the analogical argument (the hadith of the angel speaking on Umar's tongue).
The rational argument is based on the impossibility of the jinn having power over the epileptic's tongue.
3
Understand the metaphorical attribution
See how Nasafi uses the hadith to show that attributing speech to a supernatural agent is metaphorical when it is inspired, not literal.
This resolves the misconception without denying the experience of epileptics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكر من قول الناس في كلام المصروع أن الجني يتكلم على لسانه دليل الإفلاس، فإن ذلك ليس بقول من يلزم الانقياد لقوله والتعلق مثله لا يجدي نفعا. ثم نقول: إذا لم يكن لسان المصروع محلا لقدرة الجني، ومخلوق ما لا قدرة على ما هو خارج عن حيز قدرته عندنا فلا يتصور عندنا أن يكون ذلك الكلام فعلا للجني. ثم نقول : لو ثبت أن أحدا يقول ذلك يريد به أن الجني يلقي في قلب المصروع شيئا فيجرع المصروع ذلك على لسانه، فأضيف ذلك إلى الجني لكونه حاملا للمصروع على إجراء ذلك على لسانه يحققه ما روي أنه قال: "إن الملك لينطق على لسان عمر" لم يكن ذلك فعلا للملك لأنه لو كان كذلك لم يكن لعمر منقبة بل كان فعلا لعمر إلا أن الملك لما كان يلقي ذلك في قلبه حتى أظهره عمر بلسانه أضيف إلى الملك على طريق المجاز فكذا هذا، وقد روي في بعض الروايات: "إن الحق لينطق على لسان عمر" وقيل إن الحق هو الله تعالى وليس ذلك بكلام الله تعالى. وهذا مما لا خفاء به. وبالله المعونة.
And what is mentioned from the people's saying concerning the speech of the epileptic that the jinn speaks upon his tongue is a proof of bankruptcy, for that is not a saying of one whose statement must be followed, and clinging to the like of it brings no benefit. Then we say: If the tongue of the epileptic is not a locus for the power of the jinn, and a created thing has no power over what is outside its capacity according to us, then it is not conceivable according to us that that speech is an act of the jinn. Then we say: If it were established that someone says that, meaning that the jinn casts something into the heart of the epileptic, and the epileptic then utters that upon his tongue, so it is attributed to the jinn because he is the one who impels the epileptic to utter it upon his tongue – this is confirmed by what has been narrated that he (the Prophet) said: 'Indeed the angel speaks upon the tongue of Umar.' That was not an act of the angel, because if it were so, Umar would have no merit; rather it was an act of Umar, except that when the angel cast that into his heart until Umar manifested it by his tongue, it was attributed to the angel metaphorically. So also this. And it has been narrated in some narrations: 'Indeed the Truth speaks upon the tongue of Umar,' and it is said that the Truth is Allah, may He be exalted, and that is not the speech of Allah. This is something not hidden. And with Allah is assistance.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. The opponent claims that the speech of an epileptic is actually the speech of a jinn speaking through the epileptic's tongue. Nasafi begins by dismissing this as a desperate argument that carries no authority. He then provides a rational argument: the epileptic's tongue is not under the power of the jinn, so the jinn cannot produce speech through it. Next, he offers an alternative explanation: perhaps the jinn inspires something in the epileptic's heart, and the epileptic then utters it, so the speech is attributed metaphorically to the jinn because he is the cause. He corroborates this with the hadith that the angel speaks on the tongue of Umar. He explains that the angel's speech is not literally the angel's act; otherwise, Umar would have no merit. Rather, the angel inspires Umar, and Umar speaks, so the attribution is metaphorical. Similarly, the speech of the epileptic is attributed to the jinn metaphorically. He then mentions another narration attributing speech to Allah, but clarifies that this is not literal divine speech either. The passage concludes by asserting that this point is clear.

Key Terms
كلام المصروع
الجني
الملك
المجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The jinn literally speaks through the epileptic's tongue.
Correction: The speech is actually the epileptic's own speech inspired by the jinn, attributed metaphorically.

Checkpoint
What is the point of the analogy with the angel speaking on Umar's tongue?
A) To show that angels can speak through humans literally.
B) To demonstrate that speech attributed to a supernatural agent is often metaphorical, not literal.
C) To prove that Umar was a prophet.
D) To argue that the jinn are like angels.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the literal interpretation of jinn's speech through epileptics by arguing that the epileptic's tongue is not under the jinn's power and by using the hadith of the angel speaking on Umar's tongue to show metaphorical attribution.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a claim that supernatural beings are speaking through someone, do you instinctively accept it or do you, like Nasafi, demand rational evidence? How can you train yourself to think critically about such claims in your daily life?
?
The hadith about Umar shows that even righteous inspiration is attributed metaphorically. Are you ever tempted to claim divine or angelic inspiration for your own thoughts? What would it take to remain humble and attribute all good to Allah alone?
?
Nasafi dismisses the opponents' argument as 'proof of bankruptcy.' Have you ever held onto a weak argument to defend a belief you were emotionally attached to? What would it look like to honestly re-examine that belief today, even if it means admitting you were wrong?
