Refuting Ahad Hadith in Creedal Matters
Nasafi refutes a hadith-based claim using methodological principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why ahad hadith cannot override rational proof in matters of Islamic creed (aqeedah).

Core Idea
Ahad hadith yield no certainty and cannot contradict rational proof in theology.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi tackles a specific argument that claims God was silent in pre-eternity based on a hadith. He immediately dismisses it by highlighting the hadith's weak transmission and its conflict with rational evidence. This lesson will walk you through his reasoning and its methodological importance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without translation to get a feel for the language and argument flow.
Notice the use of terms like 'آحاد' and 'دليل معقول'.
2
Understand the claim being refuted
Identify the claim: that God was silent in pre-eternity. This is a theological statement attributed to 'some companions'.
3
Analyze Nasafi's refutation
Break down the refutation: (1) The hadith is ahad (isolated), (2) it contradicts rational proof, (3) ahad hadith are invalid in creedal matters because they don't yield certainty.
Note the phrase 'لا يصح الاستدلال به في الأبواب الاعتقادية'.
4
Consider the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that such a hadith must be rejected or interpreted metaphorically. Understand why interpretation (ta'wil) is allowed when a text appears to conflict with reason.
The phrase 'بل يرد أو يحمل على أن المراد منه ترك الذكر بطريق المجاز' is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكر من بعض أصحابه أن الله تعالى كان في الأزل ساكتا عندهم فقد ما يوجب بطلانه وما تعلق من الحديث فهو من الآحاد، ورد مخالفا للدليل المعقول، وما ورد بمورد الآحاد لم يصح الاستدلال به في الأبواب الاعتقادية، وإن كان في حيز الممكنات لأنه لا يوجب العلم، فكيف يمكن قبوله مع مخالفته الدليل المعقول فلا يقبل ولا يعتقد ظاهره، بل يرد أو يحمل على أن المراد منه ترك الذكر بطريق المجاز. والله الموفق.
And what has been mentioned by some of their companions that God Almighty was in pre-eternity silent according to them, it is nullified. And what is attached from the hadith, it is from ahad reports. And it is rejected because it contradicts the rational proof. And what comes as ahad reports is not valid to be used as evidence in creedal matters, even if it is among possibilities, because it does not yield certainty. So how can it be accepted while contradicting rational proof? So it is not accepted, nor is its apparent meaning believed. Rather, it is rejected or interpreted as meaning the abandonment of remembrance by way of metaphor. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage refutes a specific argument that God was silent in pre-eternity based on a hadith. The author dismisses it by noting that the hadith is ahad (isolated) and thus cannot be used in theological matters that require certainty. And even if considered, it must be interpreted metaphorically.

Key Terms
آحاد
دليل معقول
أبواب اعتقادية
مجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any hadith can be used as evidence in aqeedah even if it contradicts rational proofs.
Correction: Ahad hadith do not yield certainty and cannot override rational evidence in creedal matters. They must be rejected or interpreted metaphorically.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi reject the hadith claiming God was silent in pre-eternity?
A) Because it is a fabricated hadith.
B) Because it is a mutawatir hadith.
C) Because it is a hadith ahad that contradicts rational proof.
D) Because it is only found in Shia sources.

Key Takeaway
Ahad hadith cannot be used to establish creedal doctrines, especially when they contradict rational proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about Allah based on a narration you heard without verifying its certainty? What will you do now to ensure your beliefs are built on certainty?
?
If a weak hadith aligns with your desires but your reason tells you otherwise, will you still cling to it? How does this lesson force you to prioritize rational proof over weak transmitted reports?
?
Nasafi says such hadith should be rejected or interpreted metaphorically. Is there a specific belief you hold that you have never critically examined? Will you today subject it to this standard?

The Quran Is Not Identical to Human Recitation
Nasafi refutes the identity of Quran and recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran cannot be identical to recitation and how Nasafi uses reductio ad absurdum to refute this claim.

Core Idea
The Quran is not the same as recitation; identity would make it self-causing.

In this passage, Nasafi begins by addressing a fundamental confusion: some scholars equate the Quran with the audible recitation. He argues that this is impossible because a thing cannot be the cause of its own existence. He then warns that such a claim leads to absurd consequences, such as allowing any quality to appear at recitation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to grasp the flow. Note the use of logical conditionals.
2
Identify the central claim and the reductio
Notice how Nasafi first rejects the identity claim, then if the opponent retreats to saying Quran is other than recitation, he shows that contradicts their own earlier statement. Then he uses an analogy to absurdity.
3
Reflect on the principle 'a thing cannot be cause of itself'
This is a key axiom in kalam. Understand why it applies here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القرآن وهو نفسها، لأن الشيء لا يكون علة لوجود نفسه. وإن قال: القرآن غير قراءتنا. فقد ترك مذهبه، لأنه زعم أن هذا المسموع من قراءة القارئ هو القرآن، ولا يسمع إلا صوت القارئ، فأما ما كانت القراءة علة لثبوته، فلا يسمع. فإن جاز لك أن تقول: وجد عند قراءة القارئ في محل قراءته كلام، جاز لغيرك أن يدعي حدوث لون هناك أو رائحة أو طعم، وإذا كان ذلك باطلا لتعذر الوقوف عليه فكذا ما تدعون. ثم نقول: إن كان القرآن غير قراءته وكتابته، ولم يكن قبل هذا في هذا المحل، ثم وجد عند وجود القراءة والكتابة، أوجد ابتداء بأن اخترعه الله تعالى في هذا المحل أم انتقل إلى هذا المحل من محل آخر؟ فإن قال: وجد ابتداء باختراع الله تعالى وتخليقه إياه فيه. فقد جعل فعل نفسه علة لوجود فعل الله تعالى والمعلول يثبت ضرورة بلا اختيار عند ثبوت العلة، فقد جعل للعبد قدرة [؟] إلى الله تعالى إلى الأفعال. وما فيه من الفساد لا يخفي على ذي عقل. والثاني أن القرآن عندهم كان قد حدث قبل هذا في الأمكنة الأخر، وحدوث ما حدث مرة محال إلا بالإعادة، ولا إعادة إلا بعد العدم، ولم يكن القرآن انعدم. وإن قال بالانتقال فقد أحال، لأن ما لا بقاء له لا يتصور انتقاله، وقد بينا أن القول ببقاء الكلام الحادث محال على ما قررنا، ولأن الكلام عندهم حروف وأصوات، والقول ببقائه يبطل فائدة الكلام، فإن الحروف إذا بقيت وسمعها السامع جملة لا على سبيل الترادف في الوجود، لا يدري إذا سمع زيدا أنه زيد أو زدي أو بزد أو يدز أو دزي أو ديز. وهذا باطل. ولأن الانتقال من مكان إلى مكان من صفة الأجسام وهو مستحيل على الأعراض، لأن الانتقال عرض حادث فيما لم يكن متنقلا، والعرض غير قابل للعرض. ثم نقول له: هلا جوزت بغير هذه العلة وجود الجسم في مكانين، فإن علة وجود الجسم هو الكون، ولا مضادة بين الكون في هذا المكان والكون في مكان آخر، لانعدام جريان المضادة عندكم في مقتضى الجنس كالسواد والبياض، فكذا بين كون وكون فيجوز وجوده في مكانين، وكذا يلزم هذا في كل عرض متعين السواد، فنقول: كان ينبغي أن يجوز وجود سواد في أمكنة كثيرة لأن وجوده في مكان، إما أن كان لا لعلة كما يقول المتأخرون منكم، فيجوز وجوده في الثاني والثالث لا لعلة وإما أن كان لكون هو ذاته، وذاته لا تختلف في حق الأمكنة، لانعدام علة الاختصاص وراء ذاته واندفع كلامه وبالله التوفيق.
The Quran is itself [i.e., identical to recitation], because a thing cannot be the cause of its own existence. And if he says: The Quran is other than our recitation, then he has abandoned his doctrine, because he claimed that this audible from the recitation of the reciter is the Quran, and nothing is heard except the voice of the reciter. As for that for which recitation is the cause of its establishment, it is not heard. So if it is permissible for you to say: There came into existence at the recitation of the reciter in the place of his recitation speech, it would be permissible for another to claim the occurrence of a color there, or a smell, or a taste. And if that is false because it is impossible to verify, then likewise what you claim [is false]. Then we say: If the Quran is other than his recitation and his writing, and it was not before this in this place, then it came into existence at the existence of recitation and writing, did it come into existence initially by Allah creating it in this place, or did it transfer to this place from another place? If he says: It came into existence initially by Allah's invention and His creation of it in it, then he has made his own act a cause for the existence of Allah's act, and the effect exists necessarily without choice upon the existence of the cause. So he has made for the servant power [?] to Allah for actions. What corruption this contains is not hidden from one of intellect. And the second [possibility] is that the Quran, according to them, had occurred before this in other places, and the occurrence of what has occurred once is impossible except by repetition, and there is no repetition except after non-existence, and the Quran had not become non-existent. And if he says by transfer, he has deemed it impossible, because what has no duration cannot be conceived to transfer. And we have explained that the statement of the permanence of originated speech is impossible according to what we have established. And because speech, according to them, is letters and sounds, and the statement of its permanence nullifies the benefit of speech. For if the letters remain and the hearer hears them all at once, not sequentially in existence, he would not know, when he hears 'Zayd', whether it is Zayd or Zayd [reversed] or bzd or ydz or dzy or dyz. And this is false. And because transfer from place to place is a property of bodies, and it is impossible for accidents, because transfer is an accident that occurs in what was not transferring, and an accident is not receptive of an accident. Then we say to him: Why did you not permit, by another cause, the existence of a body in two places? For the cause of the existence of a body is [its] being-in-a-place (al-kawn), and there is no opposition between being-in-this-place and being-in-another-place, due to the lack of opposition running, according to you, in the requirement of the genus, like blackness and whiteness. So likewise between one being-in-a-place and another [i.e., being in this place and that], so its existence in two places is permissible. And likewise this is necessary for every determinate accident like blackness. So we say: It would be fitting to permit the existence of blackness in many places, because its existence in a place either is not due to a cause, as the later ones among you say, so its existence in the second and third is permissible without a cause; or it is due to its being-in-a-place that is its essence, and its essence does not differ with respect to places, due to the lack of a cause of specification beyond its essence. And his speech is refuted, and with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an opponent's claim regarding the Quran and its relation to human recitation. The author begins by addressing a claim: if someone asserts that the Quran is identical to our recitation, this is impossible because a thing cannot be the cause of its own existence. If the opponent retracts and says the Quran is other than our recitation, the author points out that this contradicts the opponent's own statement that the audible recitation is the Quran. The author then uses a reductio ad absurdum: if one can claim that speech comes into existence at the place of recitation, then another could claim a color, smell, or taste there – all false. The author presents a dilemma: if the Quran is other than recitation and appears at the moment of recitation, either it is created anew by Allah in that place, or it transfers from another place. The first option makes human action a cause for Allah's act, implying compulsion and giving the servant power over Allah – corrupt. The second option is impossible because what has no duration cannot transfer, and originated speech cannot persist. Moreover, if letters persisted and were heard all at once, communication would be impossible. The author also argues that transfer is a property of bodies, not accidents, and that an accident cannot bear another accident. Finally, the author uses the opponent's own principles about no opposition between being-in-a-place and another to argue that a body could exist in two places, and similarly an accident like blackness could exist in multiple places. He concludes that the opponent's speech is refuted, with divine success.

Key Terms
القرآن
القراءة
العلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran is identical to the recited sounds.
Correction: The Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, while recitation is a human act; they are distinct.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why is it false to say the Quran is identical to recitation?
A) Because the Quran is uncreated
B) Because a thing cannot be cause of itself
C) Because recitation is not audible
D) Because the Quran transfers

Key Takeaway
The Quran is not the same as human recitation; equating them leads to logical absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you feel you are producing sounds, or do you sense you are conveying the eternal speech of Allah? What would change in your heart if you truly internalized that your recitation is not the Quran itself but a means to connect to something greater?
?
If the Quran is not caused by your recitation, then your recitation is a gift to access the uncreated. Does this make you more humble and attentive when you recite, or do you still fall into routine? How can you increase your awareness right now?
?
Have you ever felt proud of your recitation? How does the truth that the Quran is beyond your performance challenge that pride? Will you let this reshape your intention the next time you open the Book?

The Dilemma: Creation or Transfer?
Nasafi presents and refutes the creation horn of the dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possibilities Nasafi presents for the Quran's appearance at recitation and why the creation option is untenable.

Core Idea
If the Quran is other than recitation, it must be created or transferred; creation leads to compulsion.

In this passage, Nasafi presents the opponent with a dilemma. If the Quran is not identical to recitation but appears at the moment of recitation, there are only two possibilities: it is either created anew by Allah in that place, or it transfers from another place. He proceeds to show why creation is impossible, as it would make human action a cause for divine action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the dilemma
Look for the two options Nasafi presents.
2
Examine the refutation of the first option (creation)
Note how he argues that creation implies human act causes Allah's act, leading to compulsion.
3
Reflect on the theological implications
Consider why making human action a cause for divine action is corrupt in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القرآن وهو نفسها، لأن الشيء لا يكون علة لوجود نفسه. وإن قال: القرآن غير قراءتنا. فقد ترك مذهبه، لأنه زعم أن هذا المسموع من قراءة القارئ هو القرآن، ولا يسمع إلا صوت القارئ، فأما ما كانت القراءة علة لثبوته، فلا يسمع. فإن جاز لك أن تقول: وجد عند قراءة القارئ في محل قراءته كلام، جاز لغيرك أن يدعي حدوث لون هناك أو رائحة أو طعم، وإذا كان ذلك باطلا لتعذر الوقوف عليه فكذا ما تدعون. ثم نقول: إن كان القرآن غير قراءته وكتابته، ولم يكن قبل هذا في هذا المحل، ثم وجد عند وجود القراءة والكتابة، أوجد ابتداء بأن اخترعه الله تعالى في هذا المحل أم انتقل إلى هذا المحل من محل آخر؟ فإن قال: وجد ابتداء باختراع الله تعالى وتخليقه إياه فيه. فقد جعل فعل نفسه علة لوجود فعل الله تعالى والمعلول يثبت ضرورة بلا اختيار عند ثبوت العلة، فقد جعل للعبد قدرة [؟] إلى الله تعالى إلى الأفعال. وما فيه من الفساد لا يخفي على ذي عقل. والثاني أن القرآن عندهم كان قد حدث قبل هذا في الأمكنة الأخر، وحدوث ما حدث مرة محال إلا بالإعادة، ولا إعادة إلا بعد العدم، ولم يكن القرآن انعدم. وإن قال بالانتقال فقد أحال، لأن ما لا بقاء له لا يتصور انتقاله، وقد بينا أن القول ببقاء الكلام الحادث محال على ما قررنا، ولأن الكلام عندهم حروف وأصوات، والقول ببقائه يبطل فائدة الكلام، فإن الحروف إذا بقيت وسمعها السامع جملة لا على سبيل الترادف في الوجود، لا يدري إذا سمع زيدا أنه زيد أو زدي أو بزد أو يدز أو دزي أو ديز. وهذا باطل. ولأن الانتقال من مكان إلى مكان من صفة الأجسام وهو مستحيل على الأعراض، لأن الانتقال عرض حادث فيما لم يكن متنقلا، والعرض غير قابل للعرض. ثم نقول له: هلا جوزت بغير هذه العلة وجود الجسم في مكانين، فإن علة وجود الجسم هو الكون، ولا مضادة بين الكون في هذا المكان والكون في مكان آخر، لانعدام جريان المضادة عندكم في مقتضى الجنس كالسواد والبياض، فكذا بين كون وكون فيجوز وجوده في مكانين، وكذا يلزم هذا في كل عرض متعين السواد، فنقول: كان ينبغي أن يجوز وجود سواد في أمكنة كثيرة لأن وجوده في مكان، إما أن كان لا لعلة كما يقول المتأخرون منكم، فيجوز وجوده في الثاني والثالث لا لعلة وإما أن كان لكون هو ذاته، وذاته لا تختلف في حق الأمكنة، لانعدام علة الاختصاص وراء ذاته واندفع كلامه وبالله التوفيق.

Commentary

The second option is impossible because what has no duration cannot transfer, and originated speech cannot persist. Moreover, if letters persisted and were heard all at once, communication would be impossible. The author also argues that transfer is a property of bodies, not accidents, and that an accident cannot bear another accident. Finally, the author uses the opponent's own principles about no opposition between being-in-a-place and another to argue that a body could exist in two places, and similarly an accident like blackness could exist in multiple places. He concludes that the opponent's speech is refuted, with divine success.

Correction: Nasafi shows this would make human recitation a cause for Allah's action, which implies compulsion and is theologically problematic.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does this change your attitude when you recite? Commit to reciting with humility, recognizing that the Quran's existence is solely by Allah's will.
?
If you believed your actions could force Allah's hand, how would that affect your trust in Him? This lesson shows the absurdity of that belief. Search your heart: are there areas where you expect Allah to respond because of your deeds? Repent of that arrogance and return to total reliance on His mercy.
?
The dilemma forces a choice between two views of the Quran's origin. Does your heart lean towards creation (taking pride in your recitation) or towards transfer (seeing it as a gift from elsewhere)? Which view makes you more grateful and humble? Resolve to adopt the latter.

The Impossibility of the Quran Transferring
Nasafi refutes the transfer possibility and extends the argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran cannot transfer from one place to another and how Nasafi uses arguments about permanence, sequence, and accident properties.

Core Idea
An accident like the Quran cannot transfer; transfer is for bodies, and speech needs sequence.

Nasafi now turns to the second horn of the dilemma: transfer. He provides several reasons why transfer is impossible, including that originated speech lacks permanence, that letters need sequence to convey meaning, and that transfer is a property of bodies, not accidents. He also turns the opponent's own principles against them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on transfer
Identify the key points: transfer requires duration, speech is letters/sounds that need sequence, transfer is property of bodies.
2
Understand the argument about permanence
Nasafi says originated speech cannot persist; without persistence, transfer is impossible.
3
Understand the argument about letters
If letters persisted and were heard all at once, we couldn't distinguish words.
4
Understand the argument about accident transfer
Transfer is an accident, and an accident cannot bear another accident. Also, the opponent's own principles allow a body in two places.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القرآن وهو نفسها، لأن الشيء لا يكون علة لوجود نفسه. وإن قال: القرآن غير قراءتنا. فقد ترك مذهبه، لأنه زعم أن هذا المسموع من قراءة القارئ هو القرآن، ولا يسمع إلا صوت القارئ، فأما ما كانت القراءة علة لثبوته، فلا يسمع. فإن جاز لك أن تقول: وجد عند قراءة القارئ في محل قراءته كلام، جاز لغيرك أن يدعي حدوث لون هناك أو رائحة أو طعم، وإذا كان ذلك باطلا لتعذر الوقوف عليه فكذا ما تدعون. ثم نقول: إن كان القرآن غير قراءته وكتابته، ولم يكن قبل هذا في هذا المحل، ثم وجد عند وجود القراءة والكتابة، أوجد ابتداء بأن اخترعه الله تعالى في هذا المحل أم انتقل إلى هذا المحل من محل آخر؟ فإن قال: وجد ابتداء باختراع الله تعالى وتخليقه إياه فيه. فقد جعل فعل نفسه علة لوجود فعل الله تعالى والمعلول يثبت ضرورة بلا اختيار عند ثبوت العلة، فقد جعل للعبد قدرة [؟] إلى الله تعالى إلى الأفعال. وما فيه من الفساد لا يخفي على ذي عقل. والثاني أن القرآن عندهم كان قد حدث قبل هذا في الأمكنة الأخر، وحدوث ما حدث مرة محال إلا بالإعادة، ولا إعادة إلا بعد العدم، ولم يكن القرآن انعدم. وإن قال بالانتقال فقد أحال، لأن ما لا بقاء له لا يتصور انتقاله، وقد بينا أن القول ببقاء الكلام الحادث محال على ما قررنا، ولأن الكلام عندهم حروف وأصوات، والقول ببقائه يبطل فائدة الكلام، فإن الحروف إذا بقيت وسمعها السامع جملة لا على سبيل الترادف في الوجود، لا يدري إذا سمع زيدا أنه زيد أو زدي أو بزد أو يدز أو دزي أو ديز. وهذا باطل. ولأن الانتقال من مكان إلى مكان من صفة الأجسام وهو مستحيل على الأعراض، لأن الانتقال عرض حادث فيما لم يكن متنقلا، والعرض غير قابل للعرض. ثم نقول له: هلا جوزت بغير هذه العلة وجود الجسم في مكانين، فإن علة وجود الجسم هو الكون، ولا مضادة بين الكون في هذا المكان والكون في مكان آخر، لانعدام جريان المضادة عندكم في مقتضى الجنس كالسواد والبياض، فكذا بين كون وكون فيجوز وجوده في مكانين، وكذا يلزم هذا في كل عرض متعين السواد، فنقول: كان ينبغي أن يجوز وجود سواد في أمكنة كثيرة لأن وجوده في مكان، إما أن كان لا لعلة كما يقول المتأخرون منكم، فيجوز وجوده في الثاني والثالث لا لعلة وإما أن كان لكون هو ذاته، وذاته لا تختلف في حق الأمكنة، لانعدام علة الاختصاص وراء ذاته واندفع كلامه وبالله التوفيق.
The Quran is itself [i.e., identical to recitation], because a thing cannot be the cause of its own existence. And if he says: The Quran is other than our recitation, then he has abandoned his doctrine, because he claimed that this audible from the recitation of the reciter is the Quran, and nothing is heard except the voice of the reciter. As for that for which recitation is the cause of its establishment, it is not heard. So if it is permissible for you to say: There came into existence at the recitation of the reciter in the place of his recitation speech, it would be permissible for another to claim the occurrence of a color there, or a smell, or a taste. And if that is false because it is impossible to verify, then likewise what you claim [is false]. Then we say: If the Quran is other than his recitation and his writing, and it was not before this in this place, then it came into existence at the existence of recitation and writing, did it come into existence initially by Allah creating it in this place, or did it transfer to this place from another place? If he says: It came into existence initially by Allah's invention and His creation of it in it, then he has made his own act a cause for the existence of Allah's act, and the effect exists necessarily without choice upon the existence of the cause. So he has made for the servant power [?] to Allah for actions. What corruption this contains is not hidden from one of intellect. And the second [possibility] is that the Quran, according to them, had occurred before this in other places, and the occurrence of what has occurred once is impossible except by repetition, and there is no repetition except after non-existence, and the Quran had not become non-existent. And if he says by transfer, he has deemed it impossible, because what has no duration cannot be conceived to transfer. And we have explained that the statement of the permanence of originated speech is impossible according to what we have established. And because speech, according to them, is letters and sounds, and the statement of its permanence nullifies the benefit of speech. For if the letters remain and the hearer hears them all at once, not sequentially in existence, he would not know, when he hears 'Zayd', whether it is Zayd or Zayd [reversed] or bzd or ydz or dzy or dyz. And this is false. And because transfer from place to place is a property of bodies, and it is impossible for accidents, because transfer is an accident that occurs in what was not transferring, and an accident is not receptive of an accident. Then we say to him: Why did you not permit, by another cause, the existence of a body in two places? For the cause of the existence of a body is [its] being-in-a-place (al-kawn), and there is no opposition between being-in-this-place and being-in-another-place, due to the lack of opposition running, according to you, in the requirement of the genus, like blackness and whiteness. So likewise between one being-in-a-place and another [i.e., being in this place and that], so its existence in two places is permissible. And likewise this is necessary for every determinate accident like blackness. So we say: It would be fitting to permit the existence of blackness in many places, because its existence in a place either is not due to a cause, as the later ones among you say, so its existence in the second and third is permissible without a cause; or it is due to its being-in-a-place that is its essence, and its essence does not differ with respect to places, due to the lack of a cause of specification beyond its essence. And his speech is refuted, and with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an opponent's claim regarding the Quran and its relation to human recitation. The author begins by addressing a claim: if someone asserts that the Quran is identical to our recitation, this is impossible because a thing cannot be the cause of its own existence. If the opponent retracts and says the Quran is other than our recitation, the author points out that this contradicts the opponent's own statement that the audible recitation is the Quran. The author then uses a reductio ad absurdum: if one can claim that speech comes into existence at the place of recitation, then another could claim a color, smell, or taste there – all false. The author presents a dilemma: if the Quran is other than recitation and appears at the moment of recitation, either it is created anew by Allah in that place, or it transfers from another place. The first option makes human action a cause for Allah's act, implying compulsion and giving the servant power over Allah – corrupt. The second option is impossible because what has no duration cannot transfer, and originated speech cannot persist. Moreover, if letters persisted and were heard all at once, communication would be impossible. The author also argues that transfer is a property of bodies, not accidents, and that an accident cannot bear another accident. Finally, the author uses the opponent's own principles about no opposition between being-in-a-place and another to argue that a body could exist in two places, and similarly an accident like blackness could exist in multiple places. He concludes that the opponent's speech is refuted, with divine success.

Correction: The Quran is an accident (speech) and cannot transfer because transfer requires a body and accidents lack duration.

Addressing Future Generations Is Not Foolish
Argues that the Prophet's address to future people is not foolish and denial is kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's address to non-existent future people is not considered foolish, and why denying this address is deemed clear disbelief.

Core Idea
Future generations are addressed by the Prophet; denial nullifies the Shari'a.

This passage tackles a critical point in Islamic theology: the validity of prophetic address to people who did not exist at the time of revelation. Using an argument from analogy (shahid to gha'ib), the author shows that such address is wise and necessary, and that rejecting it leads to the nullification of the entire religious law.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim
The passage begins by stating that the Prophet addressed future generations. Note that they were non-existent at the time of revelation, yet the Prophet's address is not considered foolish.
2
Follow the argument from analogy
The author argues that since no one calls the Prophet foolish for addressing future people, the same applies to the general principle: addressing the non-existent is not foolish.
This is an argument from the witnessed (shahid) to the unseen (gha'ib).
3
Recognize the consequence of denial
The passage then declares that whoever denies that future generations are addressed by the Prophet's speech nullifies the laws and removes all post-Prophetic humanity from obligations, which is clear disbelief.
This shows the high stakes of this theological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النبي عليه السلام خطابا لمن يوجد من أهل الفعل إلى قيام الساعة عند البلوغ وإن كانوا معدومين حال نزول الخطاب، ولم يعد ذلك سفها ولا خروجا عن الحكمة استدلالا بالشاهد فكذا ما قلنا، ومن لم يجعل لمن وجد بعد ذلك العصر مخاطبا بذلك الخطاب مع انقطاع الوحي، أبطل الشرائع وأخرج كل الخليقة بعد وفاة النبي عن لوازم الأمر والنهي وأفلتهم عن ربقة الخطاب والقول به كفر صراح.
The Prophet, peace be upon him, addressed those who exist among the people of action until the Day of Resurrection upon maturity, even though they were non-existent at the time of the revelation of the address, and he did not consider that foolishness nor a departure from wisdom, by analogy with the witnessed; so likewise what we said. And whoever does not make those who exist after that age addressed by that address, with the cessation of revelation, nullifies the laws and removes all creation after the death of the Prophet from the necessities of command and prohibition, and releases them from the yoke of address, and holding that is clear disbelief.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is a proof that addressing non-existent future people is not foolish. It begins by noting that the Prophet himself addressed people who would exist later (until Judgment Day) even though they were non-existent when the address was revealed, and no one called him foolish. This is an argument from the witnessed (shahid) to the unseen (gha'ib). The passage then declares that whoever denies that future generations are addressed by the Prophet's speech (since revelation ceased) actually nullifies the entire Shari'a and removes all post-Prophetic humanity from the obligations of command and prohibition. Such a statement is declared clear disbelief (kufr sarah).

Correction: The author considers it clear disbelief because it nullifies the Shari'a and releases people from divine obligations.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's address to all future generations is a foundational aspect of prophethood; denying it amounts to disbelief by nullifying the Shari'a.

Refuting the First Transmitted Doubt: Quranic Verses on Creation
Refuting the first transmitted doubt by analyzing two Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quranic verses cited by those who equate takwin and mukawwan do not actually support their view, and how the author exposes the metaphorical nature of the term 'creation'.

Core Idea
Calling something 'Allah's creation' is like calling it 'His power'—a metaphor, not literal.

The opponents of the Maturidi position on takwin often appeal to Quranic verses. Here, the author tackles the first such doubt, examining two key verses. He demonstrates that the language used in these verses is metaphorical, similar to how we say something is 'in Allah's power.' This careful analysis shows that the verses do not prove identity between the act of creation and the created thing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage contains citations from two Quranic verses.
2
Identify the two verses cited by the opponents
Find Quran 31:11 and 3:190-191 in the passage. Notice how the opponents use these verses to argue that 'creation' equals the created object.
3
Understand the refutation of the first verse
The author argues that calling created things 'the creation of Allah' is a metaphor, similar to calling them 'His power'. This metaphor requires evidence, and there is no consensus that it is literal in this case.
In contrast, there is consensus that 'power' is metaphorical when applied to objects.
4
Understand the refutation of the second verse
The author notes that in Quran 3:190-191, creation is presented as signs for the intelligent. This implies that the created things are distinct from the act of creation, as they are indicators pointing to the Creator.
The signs are in the creation, not identical to the act.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how both verses, when properly interpreted, do not support the opponents' claim. Instead, they reinforce the distinction between takwin and mukawwan.
This refutation is foundational for the Maturidi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبه نقلية لبعض المتكلمين] تعلق القائلون بأن التكوين والمكون واحد بشبه سمعية وشبه عقلية. فأما الشبه السمعية التي تعلقوا بها فمنها قوله تعالى: هَذَا خَلْقُ اللَّهِ فَأَرُونِ ماذا خلق الَّذِينَ مِن دُونِهِ فاستدل سبحانه وتعالى على توحده بالإلهية دون غيره بأفعاله التي أوجدها بقدرة بعد العدم، وأطلق عليها اسم الخلق، ثم أطلق اسم المصدر وإن كان جائزا على المفعول، كما يقال لمقدور الله تعالى: هذا قدرته، إلا أن ذلك مجاز لا يصار إليه إلا عن دليل، وفي القدرة إجماع ولا إجماع فيما نحن فيه. وقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ إلى قوله : رَبَّنَا مَا خَلَقْتَ هَذَا بطلا وفيه أدلة من وجوه أحدها: أنه جعل في خلق السماوات والأرض واختلاف الليل والنهار آيات وعلامات على وحدانيته لذوي العقل ليستدلوا بما فيها
Transmitted doubts of some mutakallimun: Those who say that takwin and the thing brought into existence are one cling to transmitted doubts and rational doubts. As for the transmitted doubts which they cling to, among them is His saying, the Most High: 'This is the creation of Allah, so show me what those besides Him have created' (Quran 31:11). So He, glorified and exalted, inferred His uniqueness in divinity without other than Him by His actions which He brought into existence by power after non-existence, and He applied the name 'creation' to them. Then He applied the name of the verbal noun (masdar) – although it is permissible – to the object (maf'ul), just as it is said of what Allah has power over: 'This is His power.' However, that is a metaphor which is not to be resorted to except with evidence. In the case of power, there is consensus [that it is metaphorical], but there is no consensus regarding what we are discussing. And His saying, the Most High: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth… [up to His saying] 'Our Lord, You have not created this in vain' (Quran 3:190-191). And in it there are proofs in several respects. One of them: that He made in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of night and day signs and marks of His oneness for those of intellect, so that they may derive proofs from what is in them.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage begins the author's refutation of the transmitted doubts (shubah naqliyya) used by those who equate takwin with mukawwan. The opponents had cited Quranic verses to support their view. The first verse is Quran 31:11: 'This is the creation of Allah.' The opponents argue that 'creation' here refers to the created objects, thus the act (khalq) and the object (makhluq) are the same. The author refutes this by pointing out that in the verse, Allah uses the word 'khalq' (a verbal noun) to denote the created things. This is a metaphorical usage, similar to saying 'this is Allah's power' when referring to objects subject to His power. While in the case of power (qudra) there is scholarly consensus that such phrasing is metaphorical, there is no such consensus regarding the term 'creation'. Therefore, the opponents cannot rely on this verse without additional evidence. The second verse is from Quran 3:190-191, which speaks of the creation of the heavens and earth as signs for the intelligent. The author notes that this verse contains multiple proofs, and he begins to analyze the first aspect: that the creation of the universe and the alternation of night and day are presented as indicators of God's oneness, so that people may derive proofs from them. This suggests that the created objects are distinct from the act of creation, as they are the signs, not the act itself. The passage is cut off as the author begins to elaborate.

خلق
مصدر
مفعول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Calling something 'the creation of Allah' proves that the act of creation and the created object are identical.
Correction: The author shows that such phrasing is metaphorical, like 'His power', and does not imply identity without evidence.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main objection to using Quran 31:11 as evidence that takwin and mukawwan are identical?
A) The verse is about power, not creation
B) The verse uses a metaphorical expression
C) The verse is abrogated
D) The verse refers to angels

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verses cited by opponents do not prove the identity of takwin and mukawwan because the term 'creation' in the verses is metaphorical, and the verses actually emphasize the distinction between the act and the signs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The author distinguishes between takwin (the act) and mukawwan (the object). Would you see it more as a sign pointing to the Creator rather than the final reality? The First Transmitted Proof: 'This is the Creation of Allah'
Introduction and first transmitted proof from Surah Luqman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse from Surah Luqman is used to argue that 'khalq' refers to the created thing, and why the use of the infinitive form does not necessarily imply a metaphor.

Core Idea
The Qur'an itself calls created things 'khalq', supporting the identity of takwin and mukawwan.

The author begins by presenting the first transmitted proof. In Surah Luqman, Allah says 'This is the creation of Allah...' and applies the word 'khalq' to His acts. The author explains that the infinitive form could be a metaphor for the object, but such an interpretation requires evidence and there is no consensus here, unlike the case of 'qudra'. This sets the stage for the subsequent proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the first proof
Read the opening paragraph that introduces the transmitted proofs and then the first proof from Surah Luqman. Notice how the author immediately addresses the possibility of metaphor.
2
Understand the argument from the verse
The verse says 'This is the creation of Allah'. Allah calls His acts 'khalq'. The author argues that this shows 'khalq' is the created thing, not an eternal attribute. The use of the infinitive form could be a metaphor, but that requires evidence.
The author compares this to the term 'qudra' (power) where there is consensus that it is not a metaphor.
3
Note the distinction from 'qudra'
For 'qudra', there is consensus that calling the predestined thing 'power' is a metaphor. But for 'khalq', there is no such consensus, so we take the literal meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعلق القائلون بأن التكوين والمكون واحد بشبه سمعية وشبه عقلية. فأما الشبه السمعية التي تعلقوا بها فمنها قوله تعالى: هَذَا خَلْقُ اللَّهِ فَأَرُونِ ماذا خلق الَّذِينَ مِن دُونِهِ فاستدل سبحانه وتعالى على توحده بالإلهية دون غيره بأفعاله التي أوجدها بقدرة بعد العدم، وأطلق عليها اسم الخلق، ثم أطلق اسم المصدر وإن كان جائزا على المفعول، كما يقال لمقدور الله تعالى: هذا قدرته، إلا أن ذلك مجاز لا يصار إليه إلا عن دليل، وفي القدرة إجماع ولا إجماع فيما نحن فيه. وقوله تعالى: إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ إلى قوله : رَبَّنَا مَا خَلَقْتَ هَذَا بطلا وفيه أدلة من وجوه أحدها: أنه جعل في خلق السماوات والأرض واختلاف الليل والنهار آيات وعلامات على وحدانيته لذوي العقل ليستدلوا بما فيها من علامات الحدوث على أن له محدثا أحدثه، وإنما يستدل على ذلك بمفعولاته لا بصفاته التي هي غير مرئية لنا، وما دل على الصانع فهو مصنوعه. والآخر أنه قال : وَيَتَفَكَّرُونَ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وإنما يكون التفكر فيه بالاستدلال بالصنع على الصانع، وجعل محل التفكر خلق السماوات والأرض، والعاقل يتفكر فيما يشاهد من أفعاله ليستدل به على الفاعل، فدل على أنه أراد به مفعولاته ومخلوقاته، وسماها خلقا دل على أن الخلق مخلوق. والآخر أنه قال : رَبَّنَا مَا خَلَقْتَ هَذَا بَطِلًا وهو إشارة إلى الخلق أيضا فإنه تعالى قال في أول الآية: إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السمواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ ثم قال في آخر الآية : وَيَتَفَكَرُونَ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ . فلو كان هذا الاسم مجازا للمخلوقات لما كرر هذا الاسم عليه. إذ ليس من شأن العرب التكرار في المجازات، وقوله تعالى: يَخلُقَكُمْ فِي بُطُونِ أُمَّهَتِكُمْ خَلْقًا مِنْ بَعْدِ خَلْقٍ فجعل خلقا بعد خلق والقديم لا يجوز أن يتأخر في الوجود حتى يكون قبله غيره. وقوله تعالى: أَمْ جَعَلُوا لِلَّهِ شُرَكَاة خَلَقُوا كَخَلْقِهِ فتشبه الْخَلْق عَلَيْهِمْ قُلْ اللَّهُ خَالِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ وَهُوَ الْوَاحِدُ الْقَهَّارُ يعني خالق كل خلق، وقال تعالى: ثُمَّ أَنشَأْنَهُ خَلْقًا آخَرَ وقوله تعالى: أَمَّن يَبْدَأُ الْخَلْقَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُهُ فجعل للخلق ابتداء وإعادة وكل واحد منهما دليل الحدوث. وقال تعالى : لَخَلْقُ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ أَكْبَرُ مِنْ خَلْقِ النَّاسِ وما وصف بالقدم لا يوصف بالأكبر والأصغر. وقوله تعالى خبرا عن إبليس عليه اللعنة: وَلَا آمُرَهُمْ
Those who say that takwin (bringing into existence) and the mukawwan (thing brought into existence) are one have attached themselves to transmitted proofs (shubah sam'iyya) and rational proofs. As for the transmitted proofs they have attached themselves to, among them is His saying, the Exalted: 'This is the creation of Allah, so show me what those other than Him have created.' So He, glorified and exalted, argued for His oneness in divinity without other than Him by His acts which He brought into existence by power after non-existence, and He applied the name 'khalq' (creation) to them, then He applied the name of the masdar (infinitive) although it is permissible for the maf'ul (object), just as it is said for the predestined thing of Allah, the Exalted: 'this is His power,' except that that is a metaphor (majāz) which is not resorted to except with evidence, and there is consensus (ijmā') regarding power, but there is no consensus in what we are discussing. And His saying, the Exalted: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth...' up to His saying: 'Our Lord, You have not created this in vain.' In it there are proofs from several aspects: one of them is that He made in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of night and day signs and indicators of His oneness for those of intellect, so that they might infer by what is in them of signs of temporality that He has an originator who originated it, and one infers that only by His effects (maf'ulāt), not by His attributes which are invisible to us, and what indicates the Maker is His made thing (masnū'). And the other is that He said: 'And they reflect upon the creation of the heavens and the earth,' and reflection upon it is only by inferring the Maker from the making, and He made the locus of reflection the creation of the heavens and the earth, and the rational person reflects upon what he witnesses of His acts to infer the Agent, so it indicates that He intended by it His effects and His created things, and He called them 'khalq', indicating that 'al-khalq' is the created thing (makhluq). And the other is that He said: 'Our Lord, You have not created this in vain,' and it is an indication to 'al-khalq' as well, for He, the Exalted, said at the beginning of the verse: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth,' then He said at the end of the verse: 'And they reflect upon the creation of the heavens and the earth.' So if this name were a metaphor for the created things, He would not have repeated this name for them, for it is not the way of the Arabs to repeat in metaphors. And His saying, the Exalted: 'He creates you in the wombs of your mothers, creation after creation' – He made 'khalq' after 'khalq', and the eternal (al-qadīm) cannot be delayed in existence such that something else precedes it. And His saying, the Exalted: 'Or have they attributed to Allah partners who created like His creation, so the creation became confused for them? Say: Allah is the Creator of everything, and He is the One, the Subduer' – meaning the Creator of every creation. And He said, the Exalted: 'Then We produced him as another creation.' And His saying, the Exalted: 'Or who begins the creation and then repeats it?' – He made for 'al-khalq' a beginning and a repetition, and each one of them is an evidence of temporality. And He said, the Exalted: 'The creation of the heavens and the earth is greater than the creation of mankind' – and what is described by eternity (qidam) cannot be described as greater or smaller. And His saying, the Exalted, relating the story of Iblis, upon him be curse: 'And I will not command them...' [incomplete]
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage presents the transmitted proofs (shubah sam'iyya) used by those who argue that takwin (the act of bringing into existence) is identical to the mukawwan (the thing brought into existence). The author cites multiple Qur'anic verses and explains how each one indicates that the term 'khalq' refers to the created object, not to a separate eternal attribute. The first proof is from Surah Luqmān: 'This is the creation of Allah, so show me what those other than Him have created.' Allah applies 'khalq' to His acts (af'āl) that He originated after non-existence, using the masdar (infinitive) form, which could be a metaphor for the maf'ul (object), but such metaphor requires evidence, and there is no consensus here unlike the case of 'qudra' (power). The second proof is from the āyat of Surah Āl-Imrān: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth...' The author extracts three arguments from this verse: (a) Allah made the act of creation (khalq) a sign of His oneness, and one infers the Maker from His effects, not His invisible attributes. (b) The verse says 'they reflect upon the creation of the heavens and the earth' – reflection is on the created things (masnū'āt) to infer the Maker. (c) The repetition of the word 'khalq' at the beginning and end of the passage shows it is not a metaphor, because Arabs do not repeat metaphors. The third proof is from Surah Az-Zumar: 'He creates you in the wombs of your mothers, creation after creation.' This sequence of 'khalq' after 'khalq' cannot apply to an eternal attribute (which is not subject to temporal sequence). The fourth proof is from Surah Ar-Ra'd: 'Or have they attributed to Allah partners who created like His creation...' Here 'khalq' is used for both the act and the object, and the verse says 'Allah is the Creator (Khāliq) of every creation (khalq).' The fifth proof is from Surah Al-Mu'minūn: 'Then We produced him as another creation' – showing 'khalq' as a new originated thing. The sixth proof is from Surah An-Naml: 'Or who begins the creation and then repeats it?' – 'khalq' has a beginning and a repetition, indicating temporality. The seventh proof is from Surah Ghāfir: 'The creation of the heavens and the earth is greater than the creation of mankind' – if 'khalq' were eternal, it could not be described as greater or smaller. Finally, the eighth proof is from the story of Iblīs: 'And I will not command them...' (the verse is incomplete but implies that Iblīs's act of misguidance is created). All these proofs aim to establish that the term 'khalq' in the Qur'an refers to the created entities, thus supporting the view that takwin is identical to the mukawwan.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, why does the author argue that the term 'khalq' in the verse should not be interpreted as a metaphor?
A) Because the infinitive cannot be used for the object in Arabic.
B) Because there is no consensus that it is metaphorical, unlike the case of 'qudra'.
C) Because the verse explicitly says 'this is the creation of Allah'.
D) Because the verse is about the oneness of Allah.

Key Takeaway
The first proof uses the verse from Surah Luqman to show that 'khalq' refers to created entities, and the metaphorical interpretation is not supported by consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'This is the creation of Allah' in Surah Luqman, do you automatically think of the act of creating or the things created? Which interpretation makes you feel more awe of Allah's power—and why? From today, commit to pausing on every mention of 'khalq' in the Qur'an to reflect on what Allah is calling you to see.
?
The author insists that calling creation 'khalq' is literal, not metaphorical. Are there areas of your faith where you prefer 'metaphor' to avoid the weight of Allah's direct action? Where in your life are you explaining away God's hand as just a figure of speech? Before tonight, identify one specific blessing you have called 'luck' or 'nature' and rename it literally as 'Allah's creation' in your heart.
?
If every created thing is literally Allah's 'khalq'—His act made object—how should that change the way you treat your own body, your time, and your wealth? Pick one of these three and decide one concrete action you will take today to honor it as His direct creation.

Unseen Matters
beginner
5 min
The Second Proof: 'In the Creation of the Heavens and the Earth'
Second transmitted proof with three sub-arguments from Surah Al-Imran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three arguments derived from the verse about the creation of the heavens and the earth that demonstrate 'khalq' refers to created things.

Core Idea
Reflection upon creation leads to the Creator, and the repeated use of 'khalq' shows it is not a metaphor.

The author then cites a longer passage from Surah Al-Imran and extracts three distinct arguments. First, the verse makes the act of creation a sign of Allah's oneness, and people infer the Maker from His effects. Second, the verse speaks of 'reflection upon the creation' (khalq), which is only possible if 'khalq' refers to the created things that are witnessed. Third, the repetition of the word 'khalq' at the beginning and end of the passage indicates it is not a metaphor, as Arabs do not repeat metaphors.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof passage
Read the passage that starts with 'And His saying, the Exalted: Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth...' and ends with 'it is not the way of the Arabs to repeat in metaphors.' Identify the three arguments.
2
Identify the first argument: creation as a sign
The first argument states that Allah made the creation of the heavens and earth a sign of His oneness for those of intellect, and one infers the Creator from His effects (maf'ulāt), not from His invisible attributes.
What indicates the Maker is His made thing (masnū').
3
Identify the second argument: reflection on creation
The second argument is from the phrase 'they reflect upon the creation of the heavens and the earth'. Reflection is only possible upon something that is witnessed, i.e., the created things. So 'khalq' here means the created things.
The locus of reflection is 'khalq', so it must be the created objects.
4
Identify the third argument: repetition of 'khalq'
The word 'khalq' is repeated at the beginning and end of the verse. If it were a metaphor, the Arabs would not repeat it in this way. Thus it is used literally for the created things.
Repetition in metaphors is not Arabic practice.

(b) The verse says 'they reflect upon the creation of the heavens and the earth' – reflection is on the created things (masnū'āt) to infer the Maker. (c) The repetition of the word 'khalq' at the beginning and end of the passage shows it is not a metaphor, because Arabs do not repeat metaphors. What will you do today to ensure your recitation leads to genuine inference of the Creator from His creation?
?
The author says that reflection (tafakkur) on creation is directed at created things, not at an abstract attribute. When you look at the night sky, a mountain, or your own body, do you see them as signs pointing to Allah, or do you stop at their physical beauty? What is one specific created thing you will contemplate tonight to remind yourself of your utter dependence on the Creator?
?
The third argument highlights that repetition of a word in the Qur'an is not purposeless—it confirms literal meaning. Does this challenge your tendency to overlook repeated phrases in the Qur'an as mere emphasis? How can you change your approach to such repetitions so that they strengthen your conviction in the truth of the message?

Proofs from Sequential Creation and Created Likeness
Third and fourth transmitted proofs from Surah Az-Zumar and Ar-Ra'd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verses about sequential creation and the challenge to produce similar creation support the idea that 'khalq' is the created thing.

Core Idea
Temporal sequence and comparison of creations show that 'khalq' refers to originated objects.

The author then presents two more proofs. The verse from Surah Az-Zumar says 'He creates you... creation after creation', showing a sequence of 'khalq' after 'khalq', which cannot apply to an eternal attribute. The verse from Surah Ar-Ra'd speaks of partners who 'created like His creation', making the creation confused, then says 'Allah is the Creator of every creation', using 'khalq' for both the act and the object.

Guided Path
1
Read the third and fourth proofs
Read the passage that includes the two verses from Surah Az-Zumar and Surah Ar-Ra'd. Notice the arguments derived from each.
2
Understand the 'creation after creation' argument
The verse 'He creates you... creation after creation' implies multiple instances of 'khalq' in sequence. The eternal (qadīm) cannot be delayed or have succession, so 'khalq' must refer to temporal created things.
The author says: 'the eternal cannot be delayed in existence such that something else precedes it.'
3
Analyze the 'created like His creation' argument
The verse challenges partners who 'created like His creation', then says 'Allah is the Creator of every creation'. The word 'khalq' is used for both the act (created) and the object (creation). This indicates that 'khalq' encompasses both meanings, and in context it refers to the created entities.
The phrase 'Khāliq of every khalq' reinforces that 'khalq' is the object.

تعلق القائلون بأن التكوين والمكون واحد بشبه سمعية وشبه عقلية. فأما الشبه السمعية التي تعلقوا بها فمنها قوله تعالى: هَذَا خَلْقُ اللَّهِ فَأَرُونِ ماذا خلق الَّذِينَ مِن دُونِهِ فاستدل سبحانه وتعالى على توحده بالإلهية دون غيره بأفعاله التي أوجدها بقدرة بعد العدم، وأطلق عليها اسم الخلق، ثم أطلق اسم المصدر وإن كان جائزا على المفعول، كما يقال لمقدور الله تعالى: هذا قدرته، إلا أن ذلك مجاز لا يصار إليه إلا عن دليل، وفي القدرة إجماع ولا إجماع فيما نحن فيه. وقوله تعالى: إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ إلى قوله : رَبَّنَا مَا خَلَقْتَ هَذَا بطلا وفيه أدلة من وجوه أحدها: أنه جعل في خلق السماوات والأرض واختلاف الليل والنهار آيات وعلامات على وحدانيته لذوي العقل ليستدلوا بما فيها من علامات الحدوث على أن له محدثا أحدثه، وإنما يستدل على ذلك بمفعولاته لا بصفاته التي هي غير مرئية لنا، وما دل على الصانع فهو مصنوعه. والآخر أنه قال : وَيَتَفَكَّرُونَ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وإنما يكون التفكر فيه بالاستدلال بالصنع على الصانع، وجعل محل التفكر خلق السماوات والأرض، والعاقل يتفكر فيما يشاهد من أفعاله ليستدل به على الفاعل، فدل على أنه أراد به مفعولاته ومخلوقاته، وسماها خلقا دل على أن الخلق مخلوق. والآخر أنه قال : رَبَّنَا مَا خَلَقْتَ هَذَا بَطِلًا وهو إشارة إلى الخلق أيضا فإنه تعالى قال في أول الآية: إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السمواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ ثم قال في آخر الآية : وَيَتَفَكَرُونَ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ . فلو كان هذا الاسم مجازا للمخلوقات لما كرر هذا الاسم عليه. إذ ليس من شأن العرب التكرار في المجازات، وقوله تعالى: يَخلُقَكُمْ فِي بُطُونِ أُمَّهَتِكُمْ خَلْقًا مِنْ بَعْدِ خَلْقٍ فجعل خلقا بعد خلق والقديم لا يجوز أن يتأخر في الوجود حتى يكون قبله غيره. وقوله تعالى: أَمْ جَعَلُوا لِلَّهِ شُرَكَاة خَلَقُوا كَخَلْقِهِ فتشبه الْخَلْق عَلَيْهِمْ قُلْ اللَّهُ خَالِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ وَهُوَ الْوَاحِدُ الْقَهَّارُ يعني خالق كل خلق، وقال تعالى: ثُمَّ أَنشَأْنَهُ خَلْقًا آخَرَ وقوله تعالى: أَمَّن يَبْدَأُ الْخَلْقَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُهُ فجعل للخلق ابتداء وإعادة وكل واحد منهما دليل الحدوث. وقال تعالى : لَخَلْقُ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ أَكْبَرُ مِنْ خَلْقِ النَّاسِ وما وصف بالقدم لا يوصف بالأكبر والأصغر. وقوله تعالى خبرا عن إبليس عليه اللعنة: وَلَا آمُرَهُمْ
Those who say that takwin (bringing into existence) and the mukawwan (thing brought into existence) are one have attached themselves to transmitted proofs (shubah sam'iyya) and rational proofs. As for the transmitted proofs they have attached themselves to, among them is His saying, the Exalted: 'This is the creation of Allah, so show me what those other than Him have created.' So He, glorified and exalted, argued for His oneness in divinity without other than Him by His acts which He brought into existence by power after non-existence, and He applied the name 'khalq' (creation) to them, then He applied the name of the masdar (infinitive) although it is permissible for the maf'ul (object), just as it is said for the predestined thing of Allah, the Exalted: 'this is His power,' except that that is a metaphor (majāz) which is not resorted to except with evidence, and there is consensus (ijmā') regarding power, but there is no consensus in what we are discussing. And His saying, the Exalted: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth...' up to His saying: 'Our Lord, You have not created this in vain.' In it there are proofs from several aspects: one of them is that He made in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of night and day signs and indicators of His oneness for those of intellect, so that they might infer by what is in them of signs of temporality that He has an originator who originated it, and one infers that only by His effects (maf'ulāt), not by His attributes which are invisible to us, and what indicates the Maker is His made thing (masnū'). And the other is that He said: 'And they reflect upon the creation of the heavens and the earth,' and reflection upon it is only by inferring the Maker from the making, and He made the locus of reflection the creation of the heavens and the earth, and the rational person reflects upon what he witnesses of His acts to infer the Agent, so it indicates that He intended by it His effects and His created things, and He called them 'khalq', indicating that 'al-khalq' is the created thing (makhluq). And the other is that He said: 'Our Lord, You have not created this in vain,' and it is an indication to 'al-khalq' as well, for He, the Exalted, said at the beginning of the verse: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth,' then He said at the end of the verse: 'And they reflect upon the creation of the heavens and the earth.' So if this name were a metaphor for the created things, He would not have repeated this name for them, for it is not the way of the Arabs to repeat in metaphors. And His saying, the Exalted: 'He creates you in the wombs of your mothers, creation after creation' – He made 'khalq' after 'khalq', and the eternal (al-qadīm) cannot be delayed in existence such that something else precedes it. And His saying, the Exalted: 'Or have they attributed to Allah partners who created like His creation, so the creation became confused for them? Say: Allah is the Creator of everything, and He is the One, the Subduer' – meaning the Creator of every creation. And He said, the Exalted: 'Then We produced him as another creation.' And His saying, the Exalted: 'Or who begins the creation and then repeats it?' – He made for 'al-khalq' a beginning and a repetition, and each one of them is an evidence of temporality. And He said, the Exalted: 'The creation of the heavens and the earth is greater than the creation of mankind' – and what is described by eternity (qidam) cannot be described as greater or smaller. And His saying, the Exalted, relating the story of Iblis, upon him be curse: 'And I will not command them...' [incomplete]
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage presents the transmitted proofs (shubah sam'iyya) used by those who argue that takwin (the act of bringing into existence) is identical to the mukawwan (the thing brought into existence). The author cites multiple Qur'anic verses and explains how each one indicates that the term 'khalq' refers to the created object, not to a separate eternal attribute. The first proof is from Surah Luqmān: 'This is the creation of Allah, so show me what those other than Him have created.' Allah applies 'khalq' to His acts (af'āl) that He originated after non-existence, using the masdar (infinitive) form, which could be a metaphor for the maf'ul (object), but such metaphor requires evidence, and there is no consensus here unlike the case of 'qudra' (power). The second proof is from the āyat of Surah Āl-Imrān: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth...' The author extracts three arguments from this verse: (a) Allah made the act of creation (khalq) a sign of His oneness, and one infers the Maker from His effects, not His invisible attributes. (b) The verse says 'they reflect upon the creation of the heavens and the earth' – reflection is on the created things (masnū'āt) to infer the Maker. (c) The repetition of the word 'khalq' at the beginning and end of the passage shows it is not a metaphor, because Arabs do not repeat metaphors. The third proof is from Surah Az-Zumar: 'He creates you in the wombs of your mothers, creation after creation.' This sequence of 'khalq' after 'khalq' cannot apply to an eternal attribute (which is not subject to temporal sequence). The fourth proof is from Surah Ar-Ra'd: 'Or have they attributed to Allah partners who created like His creation...' Here 'khalq' is used for both the act and the object, and the verse says 'Allah is the Creator (Khāliq) of every creation (khalq).' The fifth proof is from Surah Al-Mu'minūn: 'Then We produced him as another creation' – showing 'khalq' as a new originated thing. The sixth proof is from Surah An-Naml: 'Or who begins the creation and then repeats it?' – 'khalq' has a beginning and a repetition, indicating temporality. The seventh proof is from Surah Ghāfir: 'The creation of the heavens and the earth is greater than the creation of mankind' – if 'khalq' were eternal, it could not be described as greater or smaller. Finally, the eighth proof is from the story of Iblīs: 'And I will not command them...' (the verse is incomplete but implies that Iblīs's act of misguidance is created). All these proofs aim to establish that the term 'khalq' in the Qur'an refers to the created entities, thus supporting the view that takwin is identical to the mukawwan.

Checkpoint
According to the third proof, why does the phrase 'creation after creation' support that 'khalq' is not eternal?
A) Because the eternal cannot be created.
B) Because the eternal cannot be delayed in existence.
C) Because the phrase implies a creator.
D) Because the verse is about wombs.

Key Takeaway
These two proofs use the concepts of temporal sequence and comparison to show that 'khalq' refers to originated, created objects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the fact that Allah created you 'creation after creation' in the womb, does this sequence of stages inspire awe in you? How does knowing that each stage is a distinct creation change your view of your own existence? What commitment can you make today to live with gratitude for being brought into existence, stage by stage?
?
If 'khalq' refers to the created object, and Allah is the Creator of every object, then nothing in your life – your wealth, your health, your relationships – is independent of His creative power. How does this truth challenge your tendency to attribute your success or failure to your own efforts? What specific area of your life do you need to surrender to Allah's sole creatorship?
?
The second verse rebukes those who attribute partners creating like Allah's creation. In what subtle ways do you 'create partners' by attributing power or causation to things other than Allah? Think of a pattern in your life where you rely more on a created means than on the Creator Himself. What step will you take this week to redirect your trust entirely to Allah?

Proofs from New Creation, Beginning and Repetition, and Greater Creation
Fifth, sixth, and seventh transmitted proofs from Al-Mu'minun, An-Naml, and Ghafir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the ideas of new creation, beginning/repetition, and comparative size support the createdness of 'khalq'.

Core Idea
The Qur'an repeatedly describes 'khalq' as something that can be begun, repeated, and compared, which is impossible for an eternal attribute.

The author continues with three short proofs. The verse from Surah Al-Mu'minun says 'Then We produced him as another creation', indicating a new originated 'khalq'. The verse from Surah An-Naml says 'Who begins the creation and then repeats it?' showing that 'khalq' has a beginning and a repetition, both markers of temporality. And the verse from Surah Ghafir says 'The creation of the heavens and the earth is greater than the creation of mankind', which cannot be said of an eternal attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the three proofs together
Read the passage that contains these three proofs in quick succession. Notice how each verse highlights a different aspect of 'khalq' as a temporal entity.
2
Understand the 'another creation' argument
The verse 'then We produced him as another creation' shows that 'khalq' can be new and distinct, which cannot apply to an eternal attribute.
'Another creation' implies a new originated thing.
3
Understand the 'begins and repeats' argument
The verse 'Who begins the creation and then repeats it?' assigns a beginning and a repetition to 'khalq'. Both are attributes of temporal things.
Each one (beginning and repetition) is evidence of temporality.
4
Understand the 'greater than' argument
The verse 'The creation of the heavens and the earth is greater than the creation of mankind' compares sizes. The eternal cannot be described as greater or smaller.
The author says: 'what is described by eternity cannot be described as greater or smaller.'

This sequence of 'khalq' after 'khalq' cannot apply to an eternal attribute (which is not subject to temporal sequence). The fourth proof is from Surah Ar-Ra'd: 'Or have they attributed to Allah partners who created like His creation...' Here 'khalq' is used for both the act and the object, and the verse says 'Allah is the Creator (Khāliq) of every creation (khalq).' The fifth proof is from Surah Al-Mu'minūn: 'Then We produced him as another creation' – showing 'khalq' as a new originated thing. The sixth proof is from Surah An-Naml: 'Or who begins the creation and then repeats it?' – 'khalq' has a beginning and a repetition, indicating temporality. The seventh proof is from Surah Ghāfir: 'The creation of the heavens and the earth is greater than the creation of mankind' – if 'khalq' were eternal, it could not be described as greater or smaller. Finally, the eighth proof is from the story of Iblīs: 'And I will not command them...' (the verse is incomplete but implies that Iblīs's act of misguidance is created). All these proofs aim to establish that the term 'khalq' in the Qur'an refers to the created entities, thus supporting the view that takwin is identical to the mukawwan.

Checkpoint
According to the seventh proof, why does the comparison 'greater than' indicate that 'khalq' is not eternal?
A) Because the eternal is always the greatest.
B) Because the eternal cannot be described as greater or smaller.
C) Because the verse mentions the heavens and earth.
D) Because mankind is small.

Key Takeaway
These proofs show that 'khalq' has properties of originated things (newness, beginning, repetition, comparability) that cannot apply to an eternal attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the sky or your own body, do you see them as 'greater' than other creations? This lesson teaches that the heavens and earth are described as 'greater' in creation, but that comparison only applies to created things. It reminds you that everything you see is contingent and originated. Does your heart truly feel that everything is created by Allah and not eternal? Or do you sometimes act as if the world has always been here? Reflect on one habit that shows you forget the temporality of this world, and commit to a specific action to remember that Allah alone is eternal.
?
The Qur'an uses the word 'another' for the creation of man. Your own existence is an act of Allah's new creation. Do you live with the awareness that you were brought into existence from nothing, and that your life is a fresh creation every moment? How would your gratitude or humility change if you truly believed that? Identify one moment today when you can pause and say, 'Allah created me anew just now.'
?
The verse says: 'Who begins the creation and then repeats it?' – your life is a repetition of creation each day. But do you live as if this moment is the only one that matters? What would change in your priorities if you truly believed that Allah is constantly re-creating you and that every breath is a new beginning?

The Eighth Proof: The Story of Iblis (Incomplete)
Eighth transmitted proof from the story of Iblis (incomplete).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the incomplete proof from the story of Iblis that is used to argue that 'khalq' refers to created acts.

Core Idea
Even the actions of Iblis are created, showing 'khalq' encompasses all created things.

The final transmitted proof cited by the author is from the story of Iblis, where Allah says regarding him: '...And I will not command them...' The verse is incomplete in the text, but the implication is that Iblis's act of misguidance is also a creation, further supporting that 'khalq' refers to created entities. However, due to the incomplete nature, the full argument is not fully presented.

Guided Path
1
Read the incomplete passage
Read the short fragment that references the story of Iblis. Note that the verse is cut off, but the intended argument can be inferred from the context.
2
Understand the intended argument
The author likely intended to show that even the actions of Iblis are created objects, hence 'khalq' includes human acts. However, without the complete verse, the argument remains ambiguous.
The reconstruction is: 'And I will not command them...'
